Claude responded: Azul AlphaZero → Value Net Learning — Project Plan
Azul AlphaZero → Value Net Learning — Project Plan

    Status: Phase redesign complete (pivot from AlphaZero to supervised value learning) Last updated: 2026-05-08 Goal: Build a superhuman Azul bot via learned value function + AlphaBeta search

Vision Shift

Original goal: AlphaZero-style self-play training → strong bot

Reality: Neural policy head stagnated (gen 1–2). MCTS distributions near-random. Training signal corrupted.

New approach: Abandon policy learning. Use supervised value learning instead.

    AlphaBeta search provides ground-truth position evaluation
    Train neural value net to match AB evaluations
    Integrate learned value into AB search
    Iterate: each generation's net produces better supervision for the next

Expected outcome: 90%+ win rate vs AB hard. Superhuman Azul play.
Architecture: AlphaBeta + Learned Value

Classical AlphaBeta search with two evaluation options:

Hand-Coded Eval (baseline):
  value = player.earned_differential (current score advantage)
  
Learned Value (gen-0+):
  encoding = encode_game(position)
  value = value_net(encoding)  [trained on AB supervision]
  
Integration:
  AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, threshold=8, net_path="gen_0000.pt")
    ├─ Searches to depth 3 or until round boundary
    ├─ Uses net prediction at leaf nodes (instead of hand-coded eval)
    └─ Returns best move

Why this works:

    AlphaBeta is fast, deterministic, correct
    Hand-coded eval has constant signal but limited strategic understanding
    Neural value net learns to refine evaluation (cleanness, column strategy, end-game dynamics)
    Generational improvement: gen-1 net sees better AB evaluations, produces better supervision for gen-2

Feature Engineering (OPEN — Requires Bigger Screen)
Locked-In Features (Total: ~189 values base encoder)

Tier 1: Column Completion (Strategic Priority)

    5 column completion ratios (per column, normalized to 0.0–1.0)
    My max column completion
    My second-max column completion
    Opponent max column completion
    Opponent second-max column completion
    Rationale: Columns drive Azul scoring; 5 tiles auto-adjacent

Tier 2: Row Completion

    5 row completion ratios (per row, normalized by row capacity)
        Row 1 capacity = 1, Row 2 capacity = 2, ..., Row 5 capacity = 5
    My top-3 row completion values
    Opponent top-3 row completion values
    Rationale: Rows 1–2 are cheap early-game; row bonuses are meaningful

Tier 3: Color Completion

    5 color completion ratios (per color, normalized to 0.0–1.0)
    My max color completion
    Opponent max color completion
    Rationale: Color bonuses sneak up; less critical than columns/rows

Tier 4: Pattern Line Health

    Pattern line cleanness per row (1.0 if wall color not yet placed, 0.0 if blocked)
        5 values for me + 5 for opponent
    Pattern line fill ratio per row (current tiles / capacity)
        5 values for me + 5 for opponent
    Pattern lines that will be empty next round (1.0 if won't complete this round)
        5 values for me + 5 for opponent
    Total tiles on pattern lines / 15 (capacity crunch indicator)
        1 value for me + 1 for opponent
    Rationale: Knowing which lines are "safe" vs "trapped" vs "overcommitted" is crucial

Tier 5: Pattern Line Flexibility

    Count of incomplete pattern lines per color (flags multi-line risk)
        5 values for me + 5 for opponent
    Rationale: Starting the same color twice is usually wasteful; flags trap states

Tier 6: First-Player Tile & Game End

    I hold first-player token (1.0 / 0.0)
    Opponent holds first-player token (1.0 / 0.0)
    Can I end the game this round? (1.0 / 0.0)
    Can opponent end the game this round? (1.0 / 0.0)
    Rounds remaining for me (round_number / 6, clamped)
    Rounds remaining for opponent
    Rationale: First-player controls tempo; end-game control is a huge advantage

Tier 7: Tile Availability

    Tiles remaining by color / 20 (5 values)
    Source counts by color / 5 (5 values)
    Rationale: Scarcity affects acquisition decisions

Open Implementation (Deferred until feature finalization)

Color Demand / Bottleneck Detection

    For each color: measure demand (how many rows/columns need it) vs supply
    Flag contested colors (demand > supply)
    Implementation TBD

Row 1&2 Source Concentration

    For each of rows 1 and 2: count factories with required color
    If only 1 factory has it: urgency flag
    If 2+ factories: low urgency
    Implementation TBD

First-Player Round Context

    Value of first-player varies by round (positive early, negative in final round)
    May need round-aware coefficient
    Implementation TBD

Adjacency Grid (Optional, Expensive)

    For each empty wall slot: adjacency points if placed there
    25 values for full grid
    Deferred: expensive to compute, may not be needed for gen-0

Final Encoder Size: 169+ values (TBD after implementing locked features)
Data Generation Strategy
Phase 0: Supervision Data (Days 1–2)

Algorithm: Game playthrough with exhaustive search at round boundaries
python

def generate_supervision_data(supervisor_agent, num_examples, output_file=None, threshold=5):
    """
    Generate supervision examples from random games.
    
    For smoke test (gen-0): store in RAM (< 10k examples)
    For scaling (gen-1+): stream to disk (Option 3 hybrid approach)
    
    Args:
        supervisor_agent: AlphaBetaAgent or AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue
        num_examples: target number of training examples
        output_file: if provided, stream to disk; if None, keep in RAM
        threshold: exhaustive search when <= this many moves remain in round
    
    Returns:
        training_data: list of (encoding, value) tuples (if RAM mode)
        OR output_file path (if disk mode)
    """
    training_data = []  # RAM mode (gen-0 smoke test)
    examples_collected = 0
    
    for game_idx in range(num_games_estimate):
        game = Game(seed=random())
        
        while not game.is_game_over():
            # Play randomly until near round boundary
            while not game.is_round_over():
                moves = game.legal_moves()
                game.make_move(random.choice(moves))
                game.advance(skip_setup=True)
                
                # Check: within threshold of round end?
                remaining_moves = estimate_remaining_moves(game)
                if remaining_moves <= threshold:  # threshold=5 or 6
                    # Run exhaustive AB search to round boundary
                    ab = AlphaBetaAgent(depth=999, threshold=0)  # Force full search
                    ab_tree = ab.build_complete_tree(game)
                    
                    # Extract all visited nodes
                    for node in ab_tree.all_nodes():
                        if node.was_visited:  # Skip pruned branches
                            encoding = encode_game(node.game_state)
                            value = node.value
                            
                            training_data.append((encoding, value))
                            examples_collected += 1
                            
                            # For disk streaming (gen-1+):
                            # if examples_collected % 1000 == 0:
                            #     _flush_to_disk(training_data, output_file, append=True)
                            #     training_data = []
            
            # Round boundary reached; continue to next round
            game.advance()
        
        # Game over
        if examples_collected >= num_examples:
            break
    
    # Final flush for disk mode
    if output_file and training_data:
        _flush_to_disk(training_data, output_file, append=True)
    
    return training_data if not output_file else output_file

Key points:

    Play full random games to natural termination
    When ≤ 5 moves remain in a round: exhaustive AB search (depth=999, threshold=0)
    AB's pruning is trusted: if a branch is pruned, assume generalization will also skip it
    Collect all visited nodes from the AB tree
    Transitive benefit: depth-4 search implicitly gives us depth-3, depth-2, depth-1 data

Storage modes:

    Gen-0 (smoke test): RAM-only, ~7 MB for 10k examples
    Gen-1+ (scaling): Stream to disk every 1000 examples, load via PyTorch DataLoader

Wall time estimate:

    5k examples: 1–2 hours
    10k examples: 4–6 hours (overnight acceptable)
    20k examples: 12+ hours (full day)

Smoke test approach: Start with 5k–10k, evaluate win rate. Scale up for later generations if needed.
Training Pipeline: Value Net
Phase 1: Supervised Value Learning (Days 2–4)

Architecture:
python

class AzulValueNet(nn.Module):
    """
    Neural value network for Azul position evaluation.
    
    Architecture:
      input (169) → Linear (64) → ResBlock (64) → Dropout (0.1)
                 → value_head (64 → 32 → 1)
    
    Output: Single scalar value per position
      - Represents: (my_earned - opponent_earned) / 50.0
      - Range: approximately [-3.0, 3.0]
    """
    
    def __init__(self, input_size=169, hidden_dim=64, dropout=0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.trunk = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(input_size, hidden_dim),
            ResBlock(hidden_dim),
            nn.Dropout(dropout),
        )
        self.value_head = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(hidden_dim, 32),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Linear(32, 1),
        )
    
    def forward(self, encoding):
        """
        Args:
            encoding: (batch_size, 169) tensor
        
        Returns:
            value: (batch_size,) tensor of scalar values
        """
        trunk_out = self.trunk(encoding)
        value = self.value_head(trunk_out).squeeze(-1)
        return value

Training Loop:
python

def train_value_net(train_loader, val_loader, max_epochs=200, 
                    early_stopping_patience=20, lr=1e-3, 
                    save_dir="checkpoints/gen_0000/", device='cuda'):
    """
    Supervised training: minimize MSE between net predictions and AB labels.
    
    Args:
        train_loader: DataLoader with (encoding, ab_value) pairs
        val_loader: DataLoader for validation
        max_epochs: maximum epochs (early stopping usually stops earlier)
        early_stopping_patience: stop if val_loss doesn't improve for N epochs
        lr: learning rate
        save_dir: where to save checkpoint and logs
        device: 'cuda' or 'cpu'
    
    Returns:
        best_checkpoint_path: path to model with best val_loss
    """
    net = AzulValueNet(input_size=169).to(device)
    optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(net.parameters(), lr=lr)
    loss_fn = nn.MSELoss()
    
    best_val_loss = float('inf')
    patience_counter = 0
    training_log = []
    
    for epoch in range(max_epochs):
        # ========== Training Phase ==========
        net.train()
        train_loss = 0.0
        
        for batch_encoding, batch_values in train_loader:
            batch_encoding = batch_encoding.to(device)
            batch_values = batch_values.to(device)
            
            optimizer.zero_grad()
            pred = net(batch_encoding)
            loss = loss_fn(pred, batch_values)
            loss.backward()
            optimizer.step()
            train_loss += loss.item()
        
        train_loss /= len(train_loader)
        
        # ========== Validation Phase ==========
        net.eval()
        val_loss = 0.0
        val_mae = 0.0
        val_preds = []
        val_targets = []
        
        with torch.no_grad():
            for batch_encoding, batch_values in val_loader:
                batch_encoding = batch_encoding.to(device)
                batch_values = batch_values.to(device)
                
                pred = net(batch_encoding)
                loss = loss_fn(pred, batch_values)
                val_loss += loss.item()
                val_mae += torch.abs(pred - batch_values).mean().item()
                
                val_preds.extend(pred.cpu().numpy())
                val_targets.extend(batch_values.cpu().numpy())
        
        val_loss /= len(val_loader)
        val_mae /= len(val_loader)
        
        # Compute Pearson correlation
        val_preds = np.array(val_preds)
        val_targets = np.array(val_targets)
        val_correlation = np.corrcoef(val_preds, val_targets)[0, 1]
        if np.isnan(val_correlation):
            val_correlation = 0.0
        
        # ========== Logging ==========
        log_entry = {
            'epoch': epoch,
            'train_loss': train_loss,
            'val_loss': val_loss,
            'val_mae': val_mae,
            'val_correlation': val_correlation,
            'learning_rate': lr,
        }
        training_log.append(log_entry)
        
        print(f"Epoch {epoch:3d} | train_loss={train_loss:.4f} | val_loss={val_loss:.4f} | "
              f"mae={val_mae:.4f} | corr={val_correlation:.3f}")
        
        # ========== Early Stopping ==========
        if val_loss < best_val_loss:
            best_val_loss = val_loss
            patience_counter = 0
            best_checkpoint = f"{save_dir}/best_checkpoint.pt"
            torch.save(net.state_dict(), best_checkpoint)
            print(f"  → New best val_loss={val_loss:.4f}, saved checkpoint")
        else:
            patience_counter += 1
            if patience_counter >= early_stopping_patience:
                print(f"Early stopping at epoch {epoch} (patience exhausted)")
                break
    
    # ========== Save Summary ==========
    os.makedirs(save_dir, exist_ok=True)
    
    # Save training log
    import csv
    with open(f"{save_dir}/training_log.csv", 'w', newline='') as f:
        writer = csv.DictWriter(f, fieldnames=training_log[0].keys())
        writer.writeheader()
        writer.writerows(training_log)
    
    # Save summary
    with open(f"{save_dir}/summary.txt", 'w') as f:
        f.write(f"Generation Training Summary\n")
        f.write(f"Best epoch: {training_log.index(min(training_log, key=lambda x: x['val_loss']))}\n")
        f.write(f"Best val_loss: {best_val_loss:.6f}\n")
        f.write(f"Final train_loss: {training_log[-1]['train_loss']:.6f}\n")
        f.write(f"Final val_correlation: {training_log[-1]['val_correlation']:.4f}\n")
        f.write(f"Total epochs: {len(training_log)}\n")
    
    # Generate plots
    plot_training_curves(training_log, save_dir)
    
    return best_checkpoint

Hyperparameters:

    Input size: 169 (encoder size, TBD)
    Hidden dim: 64 (small, effective)
    Dropout: 0.1 (mild regularization)
    Learning rate: 1e-3 (standard for supervised regression)
    Batch size: 128
    Train/val split: 80/20
    Max epochs: 200
    Early stopping patience: 20 epochs

Logging (per epoch):

    train_loss, val_loss, val_mae, val_correlation, learning_rate
    Save to CSV: checkpoints/gen_NNNN/training_log.csv

Checkpointing:

    Save best checkpoint at lowest val_loss
    Save final summary: summary.txt (best_epoch, best_val_loss, final_metrics)

Visualization (post-training):

    loss_curves.png — train vs val loss over epochs
    metrics_curves.png — val MAE + val correlation
    All generated by matplotlib, saved to checkpoints/gen_NNNN/

Evaluation & Generational Loop
Phase 2: Evaluation (Every generation)

Test 1: vs Hand-Coded AlphaBeta
python

def evaluate_agents(agent_a, agent_b, num_mirror_pairs=100, verbose=True):
    """
    Run mirrored pair evaluation.
    
    For each pair:
      Game 1: agent_a (player 0) vs agent_b (player 1), bag_seed S
      Game 2: agent_b (player 0) vs agent_a (player 1), bag_seed S (sides swapped)
    
    This controls for first-player advantage and randomness.
    
    Args:
        agent_a: first agent
        agent_b: second agent
        num_mirror_pairs: number of mirrored pairs to play (2 games per pair)
        verbose: print progress
    
    Returns:
        win_rate: fraction of games won by agent_a (0.0 to 1.0)
    """
    wins = 0
    total_games = 0
    
    for pair_idx in range(num_mirror_pairs):
        bag_seed = random()
        
        # Game 1: A vs B (A is player 0)
        game1 = Game(seed=bag_seed)
        winner1_idx = play_game(game1, [agent_a, agent_b])
        if winner1_idx == 0:
            wins += 1
        total_games += 1
        
        # Game 2: B vs A (A is player 1, sides swapped)
        game2 = Game(seed=bag_seed)
        winner2_idx = play_game(game2, [agent_b, agent_a])
        if winner2_idx == 1:  # A won (player 1 in this game)
            wins += 1
        total_games += 1
        
        if verbose and (pair_idx + 1) % 10 == 0:
            print(f"Completed {pair_idx + 1}/{num_mirror_pairs} pairs "
                  f"({total_games} games, {wins}/{total_games} wins for A)")
    
    win_rate = wins / total_games
    return win_rate

win_rate_vs_hard = evaluate_agents(
    AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=f"gen_{generation:04d}.pt"),
    AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),  # AB hard
    num_mirror_pairs=100,
    verbose=True
)

Parameters:

    Format: 100 mirrored pairs (200 games, controls for luck)
    Depth: configurable, defaults to same as supervision depth (3)
    Win rate threshold: 55% to declare "success"

Phase 3: Generational Loop (Days 5–14)
python

def generational_loop(max_generations=10):
    """
    Automated generational loop: supervise → train → eval → decide.
    
    Each generation:
      1. Generate supervision data using current best net (or hand-coded for gen-0)
      2. Train new net on supervision
      3. Evaluate new net vs baseline and vs AB hard
      4. Log results, decide if improvement warrants next generation
    
    Stopping criteria:
      - max_generations reached
      - < 2% improvement for 3 consecutive generations (plateau)
      - User keyboard interrupt (graceful stop)
    """
    win_rates = {}
    plateau_counter = 0
    
    for generation in range(max_generations):
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"Generation {generation}")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        
        # ========== Step 1: Generate Supervision ==========
        if generation == 0:
            supervisor = AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=0)
            print(f"Supervisor: Hand-coded AlphaBeta (depth=3, full search to round end)")
        else:
            supervisor = AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(
                depth=3,
                threshold=0,
                net_path=f"checkpoints/gen_{generation-1:04d}/best_checkpoint.pt"
            )
            print(f"Supervisor: gen_{generation-1:04d} value net (depth=3)")
        
        target_examples = 10000 if generation < 3 else 15000  # Scale up after smoke test
        print(f"Generating {target_examples} supervision examples...")
        
        try:
            train_data, val_data = generate_supervision_data(
                supervisor,
                num_examples=target_examples,
                output_file=None if generation == 0 else f"checkpoints/gen_{generation:04d}/train_data.pt",
                threshold=5,
            )
            print(f"Generated {len(train_data)} training examples")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during data generation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 2: Train Value Net ==========
        print(f"Training gen_{generation:04d} value net...")
        
        try:
            best_checkpoint = train_value_net(
                train_data,
                val_data,
                max_epochs=200,
                early_stopping_patience=20,
                lr=1e-3,
                save_dir=f"checkpoints/gen_{generation:04d}/",
            )
            print(f"Training complete. Best checkpoint: {best_checkpoint}")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during training. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 3: Evaluate vs Baseline ==========
        print(f"Evaluating gen_{generation:04d} vs hand-coded AB...")
        
        try:
            win_rate_baseline = evaluate_agents(
                AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=best_checkpoint),
                AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),
                num_mirror_pairs=100,
                verbose=True,
            )
            print(f"Gen {generation} vs hand-coded: {win_rate_baseline*100:.1f}%")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during evaluation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 4: Evaluate vs AB Hard ==========
        print(f"Evaluating gen_{generation:04d} vs AB hard...")
        
        try:
            win_rate_hard = evaluate_agents(
                AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=best_checkpoint),
                AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),
                num_mirror_pairs=100,
                verbose=True,
            )
            print(f"Gen {generation} vs AB hard: {win_rate_hard*100:.1f}%")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during evaluation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        win_rates[generation] = {
            'vs_baseline': win_rate_baseline,
            'vs_hard': win_rate_hard,
        }
        
        # ========== Step 5: Analyze Progress ==========
        if generation > 0:
            prev_rate = win_rates[generation-1]['vs_baseline']
            improvement = win_rate_baseline - prev_rate
            print(f"\nImprovement over gen {generation-1}: {improvement*100:+.1f}%")
            
            if improvement < 0.02:  # < 2% improvement
                plateau_counter += 1
                print(f"Plateau warning ({plateau_counter}/3)")
                if plateau_counter >= 3:
                    print(f"Plateau detected for 3 consecutive generations. Stopping.")
                    break
            else:
                plateau_counter = 0  # Reset if we see improvement
        
        # ========== Step 6: User Confirmation ==========
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        if generation < max_generations - 1:
            try:
                prompt = f"Proceed to gen {generation+1}? (y/n/skip): "
                response = input(prompt).lower().strip()
                if response == 'n':
                    print(f"Stopping at gen {generation}.")
                    break
                elif response == 'skip':
                    print(f"Skipping eval games for gen {generation+1}.")
                    # (could implement skipping here)
            except KeyboardInterrupt:
                print(f"\nInterrupted. Saving results up to gen {generation}...")
                break
    
    # ========== Summary ==========
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print(f"Training Complete")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    for gen, rates in sorted(win_rates.items()):
        print(f"Gen {gen:2d}: baseline={rates['vs_baseline']*100:5.1f}%, "
              f"hard={rates['vs_hard']*100:5.1f}%")
    
    # Find best generation
    best_gen = max(win_rates.keys(), key=lambda g: win_rates[g]['vs_hard'])
    print(f"\nBest generation: Gen {best_gen} (vs AB hard: {win_rates[best_gen]['vs_hard']*100:.1f}%)")
    print(f"Checkpoint: checkpoints/gen_{best_gen:04d}/best_checkpoint.pt")

Key decisions:

    Max generations: 10 (hard cap)
    Data per generation:
        Gen 0–2: 10k examples (speed, smoke test)
        Gen 3+: 15k–20k examples (refinement)
    Plateau detection: < 2% improvement vs previous gen, 3 times in a row
    Keyboard interrupt: Graceful stop with Ctrl+C, saves results
    Evaluation: Every generation, 100 mirror pairs vs baseline + vs hard

async def stop_training() -> Dict:
    """Signal pipeline to stop training."""

@app.post("/training/start_evaluation")

    """Signal pipeline to start evaluation."""

    """Serve plot image (loss_curves.png or metrics_curves.png)."""

    """Save training hyperparameters."""

    """Fetch current settings."""

Orchestrator: scripts/training_dashboard_worker.py

Background process that:

    Watches checkpoints/pipeline_state.json for control signals
    Detects phase changes (idle → generating, etc.)
    Runs appropriate script (generate_ab_supervision.py, train_value_net.py, evaluate_agents.py)
    Updates status.json in real-time with progress
    Handles graceful stop/pause on signal

Can be run as:
bash

python scripts/training_dashboard_worker.py

Or as a background daemon during main API startup.

Hard-Won Lessons (Updated)

Building on experience from AlphaZero phase:

    Supervised learning is simpler than RL. Ground-truth labels (AB evaluations) are reliable. No credit assignment horror.
    Value learning >> policy learning for Azul. Move selection (policy) is already solved by AlphaBeta. What's missing is position evaluation (value).
    Mirrored pairs eliminate luck. Azul has high variance (tile draws). Always use mirrored pairs for evaluation.
    Early stopping is your friend. Don't manually set epochs. Let validation loss guide training.
    Generational improvement is compounding but plateaus fast. Expect 5–10% improvement per gen early, then 1–2% later. Plateau is normal.
    Exhaustive search at round boundaries is the right data. When factories empty and pattern lines are committed, the value is much clearer. Use this high-confidence data.
    RAM vs disk trade-off. Smoke test with RAM (simple), scale to disk (robust). Start with phase 0 at 10k in-RAM.
    Batch size matters less than early stopping. 128 is fine; don't overthink it.
    Dashboard is essential for visibility. Training runs overnight; without live monitoring, you can't adjust mid-run.
    Graceful shutdown is critical. Always handle Ctrl+C cleanly. Avoid orphaned processes and corrupted checkpoints.

Deferred / Future Ideas

    Ensemble value nets — train multiple nets with different data orders, vote on evaluation
    Hybrid exploration — use value net to bias AB search tree (higher-value moves get deeper search)
    Iterative deepening — start shallow with value net, gradually deepen
    Self-play refinement — once strong value net exists, use it for AlphaZero-style self-play (optional)
    Multi-depth evaluation — train separate nets for depth-1, depth-2, depth-3 evaluations
    Transfer learning — pre-train on random games, fine-tune on AB supervision
    Hardware optimization — GPU batching for faster inference during AB search
    Live reloading — swap checkpoint during training (new net available without restart)

Notes for Implementation

    Feature engineering is open — Implement locked-in features first (169 values), test the full pipeline. Add color demand, row 1&2 urgency, etc. in gen-1+ if needed or deferred.
    Exhaustive AB search — Trust pruning. AlphaBeta's pruned branches are likely unvisitable by both AB and the learned net. If this assumption fails, switch to Minimax later.
    Early stopping is automatic — Don't manually decide when to stop training. Validation loss plateau is the signal.
    Mirrored pairs are non-negotiable — Always use them for evaluation. Luck is high in Azul; mirroring reduces variance by ~50%.
    Generational plateau is normal — Expect linear improvement early, then log-scale (asymptotic). Stop when improvement < 2% for 3 gens or hit gen-10.
    Keyboard interrupt gracefully — Allow Ctrl+C to stop training mid-loop. Save current state, don't crash.
    File-based state — Use JSON for pipeline state, CSV for logs. Persistent across server restarts, human-readable for debugging.
    Dashboard optional but valuable — Can run via CLI (train_value_generations.py), but dashboard provides visibility and control.
    Test everything — Unit tests for encoder, model, training loop, agent integration, evaluation. Integration test for full gen-0 cycle.
    Document decisions — Inline comments explaining "why supervised learning", "why exhaustive search", "why mirrored pairs", etc. Future you (or others) will appreciate it.

# Azul AlphaZero → Value Net Learning — Project Plan

> **Status:** Phase redesign complete (pivot from AlphaZero to supervised value learning)
> **Last updated:** 2026-05-08
> **Goal:** Build a superhuman Azul bot via learned value function + AlphaBeta search

---

## Vision Shift

**Original goal:** AlphaZero-style self-play training → strong bot

**Reality:** Neural policy head stagnated (gen 1–2). MCTS distributions near-random. Training signal corrupted.

**New approach:** Abandon policy learning. Use **supervised value learning** instead.
- AlphaBeta search provides ground-truth position evaluation
- Train neural value net to match AB evaluations
- Integrate learned value into AB search
- Iterate: each generation's net produces better supervision for the next

**Expected outcome:** 90%+ win rate vs AB hard. Superhuman Azul play.

---

## Architecture: AlphaBeta + Learned Value

\`\`\`
Classical AlphaBeta search with two evaluation options:

Hand-Coded Eval (baseline):
  value = player.earned_differential (current score advantage)
  
Learned Value (gen-0+):
  encoding = encode_game(position)
  value = value_net(encoding)  [trained on AB supervision]
  
Integration:
  AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, threshold=8, net_path="gen_0000.pt")
    ├─ Searches to depth 3 or until round boundary
    ├─ Uses net prediction at leaf nodes (instead of hand-coded eval)
    └─ Returns best move
\`\`\`

**Why this works:**
- AlphaBeta is fast, deterministic, correct
- Hand-coded eval has constant signal but limited strategic understanding
- Neural value net learns to refine evaluation (cleanness, column strategy, end-game dynamics)
- Generational improvement: gen-1 net sees better AB evaluations, produces better supervision for gen-2

---

## Feature Engineering (OPEN — Requires Bigger Screen)

### Locked-In Features (Total: ~189 values base encoder)

**Tier 1: Column Completion (Strategic Priority)**
- 5 column completion ratios (per column, normalized to 0.0–1.0)
- My max column completion
- My second-max column completion
- Opponent max column completion
- Opponent second-max column completion
- **Rationale:** Columns drive Azul scoring; 5 tiles auto-adjacent

**Tier 2: Row Completion**
- 5 row completion ratios (per row, normalized by row capacity)
  - Row 1 capacity = 1, Row 2 capacity = 2, ..., Row 5 capacity = 5
- My top-3 row completion values
- Opponent top-3 row completion values
- **Rationale:** Rows 1–2 are cheap early-game; row bonuses are meaningful

**Tier 3: Color Completion**
- 5 color completion ratios (per color, normalized to 0.0–1.0)
- My max color completion
- Opponent max color completion
- **Rationale:** Color bonuses sneak up; less critical than columns/rows

**Tier 4: Pattern Line Health**
- Pattern line cleanness per row (1.0 if wall color not yet placed, 0.0 if blocked)
  - 5 values for me + 5 for opponent
- Pattern line fill ratio per row (current tiles / capacity)
  - 5 values for me + 5 for opponent
- Pattern lines that will be empty next round (1.0 if won't complete this round)
  - 5 values for me + 5 for opponent
- Total tiles on pattern lines / 15 (capacity crunch indicator)
  - 1 value for me + 1 for opponent
- **Rationale:** Knowing which lines are "safe" vs "trapped" vs "overcommitted" is crucial

**Tier 5: Pattern Line Flexibility**
- Count of incomplete pattern lines per color (flags multi-line risk)
  - 5 values for me + 5 for opponent
- **Rationale:** Starting the same color twice is usually wasteful; flags trap states

**Tier 6: First-Player Tile & Game End**
- I hold first-player token (1.0 / 0.0)
- Opponent holds first-player token (1.0 / 0.0)
- Can I end the game this round? (1.0 / 0.0)
- Can opponent end the game this round? (1.0 / 0.0)
- Rounds remaining for me (round_number / 6, clamped)
- Rounds remaining for opponent
- **Rationale:** First-player controls tempo; end-game control is a huge advantage

**Tier 7: Tile Availability**
- Tiles remaining by color / 20 (5 values)
- Source counts by color / 5 (5 values)
- **Rationale:** Scarcity affects acquisition decisions

### Open Implementation (Deferred until feature finalization)

**Color Demand / Bottleneck Detection**
- For each color: measure demand (how many rows/columns need it) vs supply
- Flag contested colors (demand > supply)
- Implementation TBD

**Row 1&2 Source Concentration**
- For each of rows 1 and 2: count factories with required color
- If only 1 factory has it: urgency flag
- If 2+ factories: low urgency
- Implementation TBD

**First-Player Round Context**
- Value of first-player varies by round (positive early, negative in final round)
- May need round-aware coefficient
- Implementation TBD

**Adjacency Grid (Optional, Expensive)**
- For each empty wall slot: adjacency points if placed there
- 25 values for full grid
- Deferred: expensive to compute, may not be needed for gen-0

**Final Encoder Size:** 169+ values (TBD after implementing locked features)

---

## Data Generation Strategy

### Phase 0: Supervision Data (Days 1–2)

**Algorithm: Game playthrough with exhaustive search at round boundaries**

\`\`\`python
def generate_supervision_data(supervisor_agent, num_examples, output_file=None, threshold=5):
    """
    Generate supervision examples from random games.
    
    For smoke test (gen-0): store in RAM (< 10k examples)
    For scaling (gen-1+): stream to disk (Option 3 hybrid approach)
    
    Args:
        supervisor_agent: AlphaBetaAgent or AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue
        num_examples: target number of training examples
        output_file: if provided, stream to disk; if None, keep in RAM
        threshold: exhaustive search when <= this many moves remain in round
    
    Returns:
        training_data: list of (encoding, value) tuples (if RAM mode)
        OR output_file path (if disk mode)
    """
    training_data = []  # RAM mode (gen-0 smoke test)
    examples_collected = 0
    
    for game_idx in range(num_games_estimate):
        game = Game(seed=random())
        
        while not game.is_game_over():
            # Play randomly until near round boundary
            while not game.is_round_over():
                moves = game.legal_moves()
                game.make_move(random.choice(moves))
                game.advance(skip_setup=True)
                
                # Check: within threshold of round end?
                remaining_moves = estimate_remaining_moves(game)
                if remaining_moves <= threshold:  # threshold=5 or 6
                    # Run exhaustive AB search to round boundary
                    ab = AlphaBetaAgent(depth=999, threshold=0)  # Force full search
                    ab_tree = ab.build_complete_tree(game)
                    
                    # Extract all visited nodes
                    for node in ab_tree.all_nodes():
                        if node.was_visited:  # Skip pruned branches
                            encoding = encode_game(node.game_state)
                            value = node.value
                            
                            training_data.append((encoding, value))
                            examples_collected += 1
                            
                            # For disk streaming (gen-1+):
                            # if examples_collected % 1000 == 0:
                            #     _flush_to_disk(training_data, output_file, append=True)
                            #     training_data = []
            
            # Round boundary reached; continue to next round
            game.advance()
        
        # Game over
        if examples_collected >= num_examples:
            break
    
    # Final flush for disk mode
    if output_file and training_data:
        _flush_to_disk(training_data, output_file, append=True)
    
    return training_data if not output_file else output_file
\`\`\`

**Key points:**
- Play full random games to natural termination
- When ≤ 5 moves remain in a round: exhaustive AB search (depth=999, threshold=0)
- AB's pruning is trusted: if a branch is pruned, assume generalization will also skip it
- Collect all visited nodes from the AB tree
- Transitive benefit: depth-4 search implicitly gives us depth-3, depth-2, depth-1 data

**Storage modes:**
- **Gen-0 (smoke test):** RAM-only, ~7 MB for 10k examples
- **Gen-1+ (scaling):** Stream to disk every 1000 examples, load via PyTorch DataLoader

**Wall time estimate:**
- 5k examples: 1–2 hours
- 10k examples: 4–6 hours (overnight acceptable)
- 20k examples: 12+ hours (full day)

**Smoke test approach:** Start with 5k–10k, evaluate win rate. Scale up for later generations if needed.

---

## Training Pipeline: Value Net

### Phase 1: Supervised Value Learning (Days 2–4)

**Architecture:**

\`\`\`python
class AzulValueNet(nn.Module):
    """
    Neural value network for Azul position evaluation.
    
    Architecture:
      input (169) → Linear (64) → ResBlock (64) → Dropout (0.1)
                 → value_head (64 → 32 → 1)
    
    Output: Single scalar value per position
      - Represents: (my_earned - opponent_earned) / 50.0
      - Range: approximately [-3.0, 3.0]
    """
    
    def __init__(self, input_size=169, hidden_dim=64, dropout=0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.trunk = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(input_size, hidden_dim),
            ResBlock(hidden_dim),
            nn.Dropout(dropout),
        )
        self.value_head = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(hidden_dim, 32),
            nn.ReLU(),
            nn.Linear(32, 1),
        )
    
    def forward(self, encoding):
        """
        Args:
            encoding: (batch_size, 169) tensor
        
        Returns:
            value: (batch_size,) tensor of scalar values
        """
        trunk_out = self.trunk(encoding)
        value = self.value_head(trunk_out).squeeze(-1)
        return value
\`\`\`

**Training Loop:**

\`\`\`python
def train_value_net(train_loader, val_loader, max_epochs=200, 
                    early_stopping_patience=20, lr=1e-3, 
                    save_dir="checkpoints/gen_0000/", device='cuda'):
    """
    Supervised training: minimize MSE between net predictions and AB labels.
    
    Args:
        train_loader: DataLoader with (encoding, ab_value) pairs
        val_loader: DataLoader for validation
        max_epochs: maximum epochs (early stopping usually stops earlier)
        early_stopping_patience: stop if val_loss doesn't improve for N epochs
        lr: learning rate
        save_dir: where to save checkpoint and logs
        device: 'cuda' or 'cpu'
    
    Returns:
        best_checkpoint_path: path to model with best val_loss
    """
    net = AzulValueNet(input_size=169).to(device)
    optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(net.parameters(), lr=lr)
    loss_fn = nn.MSELoss()
    
    best_val_loss = float('inf')
    patience_counter = 0
    training_log = []
    
    for epoch in range(max_epochs):
        # ========== Training Phase ==========
        net.train()
        train_loss = 0.0
        
        for batch_encoding, batch_values in train_loader:
            batch_encoding = batch_encoding.to(device)
            batch_values = batch_values.to(device)
            
            optimizer.zero_grad()
            pred = net(batch_encoding)
            loss = loss_fn(pred, batch_values)
            loss.backward()
            optimizer.step()
            train_loss += loss.item()
        
        train_loss /= len(train_loader)
        
        # ========== Validation Phase ==========
        net.eval()
        val_loss = 0.0
        val_mae = 0.0
        val_preds = []
        val_targets = []
        
        with torch.no_grad():
            for batch_encoding, batch_values in val_loader:
                batch_encoding = batch_encoding.to(device)
                batch_values = batch_values.to(device)
                
                pred = net(batch_encoding)
                loss = loss_fn(pred, batch_values)
                val_loss += loss.item()
                val_mae += torch.abs(pred - batch_values).mean().item()
                
                val_preds.extend(pred.cpu().numpy())
                val_targets.extend(batch_values.cpu().numpy())
        
        val_loss /= len(val_loader)
        val_mae /= len(val_loader)
        
        # Compute Pearson correlation
        val_preds = np.array(val_preds)
        val_targets = np.array(val_targets)
        val_correlation = np.corrcoef(val_preds, val_targets)[0, 1]
        if np.isnan(val_correlation):
            val_correlation = 0.0
        
        # ========== Logging ==========
        log_entry = {
            'epoch': epoch,
            'train_loss': train_loss,
            'val_loss': val_loss,
            'val_mae': val_mae,
            'val_correlation': val_correlation,
            'learning_rate': lr,
        }
        training_log.append(log_entry)
        
        print(f"Epoch {epoch:3d} | train_loss={train_loss:.4f} | val_loss={val_loss:.4f} | "
              f"mae={val_mae:.4f} | corr={val_correlation:.3f}")
        
        # ========== Early Stopping ==========
        if val_loss < best_val_loss:
            best_val_loss = val_loss
            patience_counter = 0
            best_checkpoint = f"{save_dir}/best_checkpoint.pt"
            torch.save(net.state_dict(), best_checkpoint)
            print(f"  → New best val_loss={val_loss:.4f}, saved checkpoint")
        else:
            patience_counter += 1
            if patience_counter >= early_stopping_patience:
                print(f"Early stopping at epoch {epoch} (patience exhausted)")
                break
    
    # ========== Save Summary ==========
    os.makedirs(save_dir, exist_ok=True)
    
    # Save training log
    import csv
    with open(f"{save_dir}/training_log.csv", 'w', newline='') as f:
        writer = csv.DictWriter(f, fieldnames=training_log[0].keys())
        writer.writeheader()
        writer.writerows(training_log)
    
    # Save summary
    with open(f"{save_dir}/summary.txt", 'w') as f:
        f.write(f"Generation Training Summary\\n")
        f.write(f"Best epoch: {training_log.index(min(training_log, key=lambda x: x['val_loss']))}\\n")
        f.write(f"Best val_loss: {best_val_loss:.6f}\\n")
        f.write(f"Final train_loss: {training_log[-1]['train_loss']:.6f}\\n")
        f.write(f"Final val_correlation: {training_log[-1]['val_correlation']:.4f}\\n")
        f.write(f"Total epochs: {len(training_log)}\\n")
    
    # Generate plots
    plot_training_curves(training_log, save_dir)
    
    return best_checkpoint
\`\`\`

**Hyperparameters:**
- Input size: 169 (encoder size, TBD)
- Hidden dim: 64 (small, effective)
- Dropout: 0.1 (mild regularization)
- Learning rate: 1e-3 (standard for supervised regression)
- Batch size: 128
- Train/val split: 80/20
- Max epochs: 200
- Early stopping patience: 20 epochs

**Logging (per epoch):**
- train_loss, val_loss, val_mae, val_correlation, learning_rate
- Save to CSV: \`checkpoints/gen_NNNN/training_log.csv\`

**Checkpointing:**
- Save best checkpoint at lowest val_loss
- Save final summary: \`summary.txt\` (best_epoch, best_val_loss, final_metrics)

**Visualization (post-training):**
- \`loss_curves.png\` — train vs val loss over epochs
- \`metrics_curves.png\` — val MAE + val correlation
- All generated by matplotlib, saved to \`checkpoints/gen_NNNN/\`

## Evaluation & Generational Loop

### Phase 2: Evaluation (Every generation)

**Test 1: vs Hand-Coded AlphaBeta**

\`\`\`python
def evaluate_agents(agent_a, agent_b, num_mirror_pairs=100, verbose=True):
    """
    Run mirrored pair evaluation.
    
    For each pair:
      Game 1: agent_a (player 0) vs agent_b (player 1), bag_seed S
      Game 2: agent_b (player 0) vs agent_a (player 1), bag_seed S (sides swapped)
    
    This controls for first-player advantage and randomness.
    
    Args:
        agent_a: first agent
        agent_b: second agent
        num_mirror_pairs: number of mirrored pairs to play (2 games per pair)
        verbose: print progress
    
    Returns:
        win_rate: fraction of games won by agent_a (0.0 to 1.0)
    """
    wins = 0
    total_games = 0
    
    for pair_idx in range(num_mirror_pairs):
        bag_seed = random()
        
        # Game 1: A vs B (A is player 0)
        game1 = Game(seed=bag_seed)
        winner1_idx = play_game(game1, [agent_a, agent_b])
        if winner1_idx == 0:
            wins += 1
        total_games += 1
        
        # Game 2: B vs A (A is player 1, sides swapped)
        game2 = Game(seed=bag_seed)
        winner2_idx = play_game(game2, [agent_b, agent_a])
        if winner2_idx == 1:  # A won (player 1 in this game)
            wins += 1
        total_games += 1
        
        if verbose and (pair_idx + 1) % 10 == 0:
            print(f"Completed {pair_idx + 1}/{num_mirror_pairs} pairs "
                  f"({total_games} games, {wins}/{total_games} wins for A)")
    
    win_rate = wins / total_games
    return win_rate
\`\`\`

**Test 2: vs AlphaBeta Hard (Progression Tracking)**

\`\`\`python
# Every generation, also test against AB hard
win_rate_vs_hard = evaluate_agents(
    AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=f"gen_{generation:04d}.pt"),
    AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),  # AB hard
    num_mirror_pairs=100,
    verbose=True
)
\`\`\`

**Parameters:**
- Format: 100 mirrored pairs (200 games, controls for luck)
- Depth: configurable, defaults to same as supervision depth (3)
- Win rate threshold: 55% to declare "success"

### Phase 3: Generational Loop (Days 5–14)

\`\`\`python
def generational_loop(max_generations=10):
    """
    Automated generational loop: supervise → train → eval → decide.
    
    Each generation:
      1. Generate supervision data using current best net (or hand-coded for gen-0)
      2. Train new net on supervision
      3. Evaluate new net vs baseline and vs AB hard
      4. Log results, decide if improvement warrants next generation
    
    Stopping criteria:
      - max_generations reached
      - < 2% improvement for 3 consecutive generations (plateau)
      - User keyboard interrupt (graceful stop)
    """
    win_rates = {}
    plateau_counter = 0
    
    for generation in range(max_generations):
        print(f"\\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"Generation {generation}")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        
        # ========== Step 1: Generate Supervision ==========
        if generation == 0:
            supervisor = AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=0)
            print(f"Supervisor: Hand-coded AlphaBeta (depth=3, full search to round end)")
        else:
            supervisor = AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(
                depth=3,
                threshold=0,
                net_path=f"checkpoints/gen_{generation-1:04d}/best_checkpoint.pt"
            )
            print(f"Supervisor: gen_{generation-1:04d} value net (depth=3)")
        
        target_examples = 10000 if generation < 3 else 15000  # Scale up after smoke test
        print(f"Generating {target_examples} supervision examples...")
        
        try:
            train_data, val_data = generate_supervision_data(
                supervisor,
                num_examples=target_examples,
                output_file=None if generation == 0 else f"checkpoints/gen_{generation:04d}/train_data.pt",
                threshold=5,
            )
            print(f"Generated {len(train_data)} training examples")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during data generation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 2: Train Value Net ==========
        print(f"Training gen_{generation:04d} value net...")
        
        try:
            best_checkpoint = train_value_net(
                train_data,
                val_data,
                max_epochs=200,
                early_stopping_patience=20,
                lr=1e-3,
                save_dir=f"checkpoints/gen_{generation:04d}/",
            )
            print(f"Training complete. Best checkpoint: {best_checkpoint}")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during training. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 3: Evaluate vs Baseline ==========
        print(f"Evaluating gen_{generation:04d} vs hand-coded AB...")
        
        try:
            win_rate_baseline = evaluate_agents(
                AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=best_checkpoint),
                AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),
                num_mirror_pairs=100,
                verbose=True,
            )
            print(f"Gen {generation} vs hand-coded: {win_rate_baseline*100:.1f}%")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during evaluation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        # ========== Step 4: Evaluate vs AB Hard ==========
        print(f"Evaluating gen_{generation:04d} vs AB hard...")
        
        try:
            win_rate_hard = evaluate_agents(
                AlphaBetaWithLearnedValue(depth=3, net_path=best_checkpoint),
                AlphaBetaAgent(depth=3, threshold=8),
                num_mirror_pairs=100,
                verbose=True,
            )
            print(f"Gen {generation} vs AB hard: {win_rate_hard*100:.1f}%")
        except KeyboardInterrupt:
            print(f"Interrupted during evaluation. Stopping.")
            break
        
        win_rates[generation] = {
            'vs_baseline': win_rate_baseline,
            'vs_hard': win_rate_hard,
        }
        
        # ========== Step 5: Analyze Progress ==========
        if generation > 0:
            prev_rate = win_rates[generation-1]['vs_baseline']
            improvement = win_rate_baseline - prev_rate
            print(f"\\nImprovement over gen {generation-1}: {improvement*100:+.1f}%")
            
            if improvement < 0.02:  # < 2% improvement
                plateau_counter += 1
                print(f"Plateau warning ({plateau_counter}/3)")
                if plateau_counter >= 3:
                    print(f"Plateau detected for 3 consecutive generations. Stopping.")
                    break
            else:
                plateau_counter = 0  # Reset if we see improvement
        
        # ========== Step 6: User Confirmation ==========
        print(f"\\n{'='*60}")
        if generation < max_generations - 1:
            try:
                prompt = f"Proceed to gen {generation+1}? (y/n/skip): "
                response = input(prompt).lower().strip()
                if response == 'n':
                    print(f"Stopping at gen {generation}.")
                    break
                elif response == 'skip':
                    print(f"Skipping eval games for gen {generation+1}.")
                    # (could implement skipping here)
            except KeyboardInterrupt:
                print(f"\\nInterrupted. Saving results up to gen {generation}...")
                break
    
    # ========== Summary ==========
    print(f"\\n{'='*60}")
    print(f"Training Complete")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    for gen, rates in sorted(win_rates.items()):
        print(f"Gen {gen:2d}: baseline={rates['vs_baseline']*100:5.1f}%, "
              f"hard={rates['vs_hard']*100:5.1f}%")
    
    # Find best generation
    best_gen = max(win_rates.keys(), key=lambda g: win_rates[g]['vs_hard'])
    print(f"\\nBest generation: Gen {best_gen} (vs AB hard: {win_rates[best_gen]['vs_hard']*100:.1f}%)")
    print(f"Checkpoint: checkpoints/gen_{best_gen:04d}/best_checkpoint.pt")
\`\`\`

**Key decisions:**
- **Max generations:** 10 (hard cap)
- **Data per generation:** 
  - Gen 0–2: 10k examples (speed, smoke test)
  - Gen 3+: 15k–20k examples (refinement)
- **Plateau detection:** < 2% improvement vs previous gen, 3 times in a row
- **Keyboard interrupt:** Graceful stop with Ctrl+C, saves results
- **Evaluation:** Every generation, 100 mirror pairs vs baseline + vs hard

## Web Dashboard: Training Orchestration

### Phase 5b: Training Dashboard (Days 6–8, parallel to Phase 5)

**Architecture:**

\`\`\`
Frontend (Vanilla JS):
  ├─ Single-page dashboard (training_dashboard.html)
  ├─ Live polling of /training/status (every 2 seconds)
  ├─ Real-time metric updates, plots, controls
  └─ Manual start/stop/pause for each phase

Backend (FastAPI):
  ├─ Extended api/main.py with /training/* endpoints
  ├─ File-based state persistence (pipeline_state.json)
  ├─ Serves plots and generation history
  └─ Handles start/stop/pause signals

Orchestrator (Background Worker):
  ├─ Watches pipeline state file
  ├─ Runs generation → training → eval sequence
  ├─ Updates state in real-time
  └─ Graceful signal handling
\`\`\`

**Storage: File-based (per generation)**

\`\`\`
checkpoints/
├─ pipeline_state.json           ← Current pipeline state
├─ training_settings.json        ← User settings
└─ gen_NNNN/
   ├─ status.json               ← Phase, progress, metrics
   ├─ best_checkpoint.pt
   ├─ training_log.csv
   ├─ loss_curves.png
   ├─ metrics_curves.png
   ├─ summary.txt
   └─ live_metrics.json         ← Rolling window
\`\`\`

### Frontend: \`frontend/training_dashboard.html\`

Single-page HTML5 dashboard with:
- **Status card:** Current phase (idle/generating/training/evaluating), progress bar
- **Live metrics:** Games collected, epoch, train loss, val loss, correlation
- **Control panel:** Start/stop buttons for each phase (enabled based on phase)
- **Settings form:** Target examples, depth, LR, batch size (editable, saved to backend)
- **Generation table:** History of all generations with stats
- **Plots:** Loss curves and metrics curves (auto-updated)

Key features:
- Vanilla JS (no build tools needed)
- Live polling of \`/training/status\` endpoint
- Graceful error handling
- Responsive layout

async def get_training_status() -> TrainingStatus:
    """Get current pipeline status, metrics, and generation history."""

### Orchestrator: \`scripts/training_dashboard_worker.py\`

Background process that:
1. Watches \`checkpoints/pipeline_state.json\` for control signals
2. Detects phase changes (idle → generating, etc.)
3. Runs appropriate script (\`generate_ab_supervision.py\`, \`train_value_net.py\`, \`evaluate_agents.py\`)
4. Updates status.json in real-time with progress
5. Handles graceful stop/pause on signal

Can be run as:
\`\`\`bash
python scripts/training_dashboard_worker.py
\`\`\`

Or as a background daemon during main API startup.

## Hard-Won Lessons (Updated)

*Building on experience from AlphaZero phase:*

1. **Supervised learning is simpler than RL.** Ground-truth labels (AB evaluations) are reliable. No credit assignment horror.

2. **Value learning >> policy learning** for Azul. Move selection (policy) is already solved by AlphaBeta. What's missing is position evaluation (value).

3. **Mirrored pairs eliminate luck.** Azul has high variance (tile draws). Always use mirrored pairs for evaluation.

4. **Early stopping is your friend.** Don't manually set epochs. Let validation loss guide training.

5. **Generational improvement is compounding but plateaus fast.** Expect 5–10% improvement per gen early, then 1–2% later. Plateau is normal.

6. **Exhaustive search at round boundaries is the right data.** When factories empty and pattern lines are committed, the value is much clearer. Use this high-confidence data.

7. **RAM vs disk trade-off.** Smoke test with RAM (simple), scale to disk (robust). Start with phase 0 at 10k in-RAM.

8. **Batch size matters less than early stopping.** 128 is fine; don't overthink it.

9. **Dashboard is essential for visibility.** Training runs overnight; without live monitoring, you can't adjust mid-run.

10. **Graceful shutdown is critical.** Always handle Ctrl+C cleanly. Avoid orphaned processes and corrupted checkpoints.

---

## Deferred / Future Ideas

- **Ensemble value nets** — train multiple nets with different data orders, vote on evaluation
- **Hybrid exploration** — use value net to bias AB search tree (higher-value moves get deeper search)
- **Iterative deepening** — start shallow with value net, gradually deepen
- **Self-play refinement** — once strong value net exists, use it for AlphaZero-style self-play (optional)
- **Multi-depth evaluation** — train separate nets for depth-1, depth-2, depth-3 evaluations
- **Transfer learning** — pre-train on random games, fine-tune on AB supervision
- **Hardware optimization** — GPU batching for faster inference during AB search
- **Live reloading** — swap checkpoint during training (new net available without restart)

---

## Notes for Implementation

1. **Feature engineering is open** — Implement locked-in features first (169 values), test the full pipeline. Add color demand, row 1&2 urgency, etc. in gen-1+ if needed or deferred.

2. **Exhaustive AB search** — Trust pruning. AlphaBeta's pruned branches are likely unvisitable by both AB and the learned net. If this assumption breaks, switch to Minimax later.

3. **Early stopping is automatic** — Don't manually decide when to stop training. Validation loss plateau is the signal.

4. **Mirrored pairs are non-negotiable** — Always use them for evaluation. Luck is high in Azul; mirroring reduces variance by ~50%.

5. **Generational plateau is normal** — Expect linear improvement early, then log-scale (asymptotic). Stop when improvement < 2% for 3 gens or hit gen-10.

6. **Keyboard interrupt gracefully** — Allow Ctrl+C to stop training mid-loop. Save current state, don't crash.

7. **File-based state** — Use JSON for pipeline state, CSV for logs. Persistent across server restarts, human-readable for debugging.

8. **Dashboard optional but valuable** — Can run via CLI (\`train_value_generations.py\`), but dashboard provides visibility and control.

9. **Test everything** — Unit tests for encoder, model, training loop, agent integration, evaluation. Integration test for full gen-0 cycle.

10. **Document decisions** — Inline comments explaining "why supervised learning", "why exhaustive search", "why mirrored pairs", etc. Future you (or others) will appreciate it.

Claude responded: Great question.

Great question. Let me think through the architecture for feature calculation.
Current Situation

Right now, _encode_flat_game_tiles() in neural/encoder.py directly accesses game state:
python

def _encode_flat_game_tiles(game: Game) -> np.ndarray:
    encoding = np.zeros(169, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Direct access to game.players, game.wall, game.pattern_lines, etc.
    encoding[0:25] = game.players[0].wall.flatten()
    encoding[25:50] = game.players[0].pattern_lines...
    # ... etc, all inline
    
    return encoding

Problem with scaling: As we add 44+ new features, this function becomes a 300-line monster. Hard to test, maintain, debug.
Three Architecture Options
Option A: Feature Extraction Helper Methods (Recommended for now)

Break feature calculation into named helper methods on Game or a new FeatureExtractor class:
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    """Extract calculated features from game state."""
    
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
    
    # Tier 1: Column completion
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for current player."""
        player = self.game.players[0]
        ratios = []
        for col in range(5):
            filled = sum(player.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
            ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
        return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for opponent."""
        player = self.game.players[1]
        ratios = []
        for col in range(5):
            filled = sum(player.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
            ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
        return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def my_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best column completion for current player."""
        return np.max(self.column_completion_ratios())
    
    def my_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: second-best column completion."""
        ratios = self.column_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])  # Efficient 2nd largest
    
    # Tier 2: Row completion
    def row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row for current player."""
        player = self.game.players[0]
        ratios = []
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = sum(player.wall[row])
            ratios.append(filled / capacity)
        return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def my_top_3_rows(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """3 values: top 3 row completion ratios."""
        ratios = self.row_completion_ratios()
        return np.array(np.partition(ratios, -3)[-3:], dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Tier 4: Pattern line health
    def pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if wall color not placed, 0.0 if blocked."""
        player = self.game.players[0]
        cleanness = []
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            has_in_wall = player.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
            cleanness.append(0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0)
        return np.array(cleanness, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: current fill / capacity per row."""
        player = self.game.players[0]
        fills = []
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = len(player.pattern_lines[row])
            fills.append(filled / capacity)
        return np.array(fills, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: total tiles on pattern lines / 15."""
        player = self.game.players[0]
        total = sum(len(player.pattern_lines[row]) for row in range(5))
        return total / 15.0
    
    # ... more methods for each feature group
    
    def extract_all_calculated_features(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Assemble all calculated features into a single array."""
        features = []
        
        # Tier 1: Columns (14 values)
        features.extend(self.column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        
        # Tier 2: Rows (16 values)
        features.extend(self.row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.extend(self.my_top_3_rows())  # 3
        features.extend(self.opponent_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_top_3_rows())  # 3
        
        # ... more tiers
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)

Then in encoder:
python

def _encode_flat_game_tiles(game: Game) -> np.ndarray:
    encoding = np.zeros(189, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Original 125 values
    encoding[0:125] = _encode_flat_original_125(game)
    
    # Calculated features (64 values)
    extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
    calculated = extractor.extract_all_calculated_features()
    encoding[125:125+len(calculated)] = calculated
    
    return encoding

Pros:

    Clear, testable, maintainable
    Each feature method is simple and well-named
    Easy to debug ("column completion is wrong" → look at one method)
    No matrix overhead (straightforward loops)
    Can test each feature independently

Cons:

    Lots of small methods
    Some overhead from method calls (negligible for 50+ features)

Option B: Pure NumPy/Matrix Approach

Pre-compute wall and pattern line as matrices, use vectorized operations:
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
        self.player = game.players[0]
        self.opponent = game.players[1]
        
        # Materialize state as matrices (one-time cost per encoding)
        self.my_wall = np.array(self.player.wall, dtype=np.int32)  # (5, 5)
        self.opp_wall = np.array(self.opponent.wall, dtype=np.int32)  # (5, 5)
    
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Vectorized: sum along rows, divide by 5."""
        filled_per_col = np.sum(self.my_wall, axis=0)  # (5,)
        return (filled_per_col / 5.0).astype(np.float32)
    
    def row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Vectorized: sum along cols, divide by capacity."""
        filled_per_row = np.sum(self.my_wall, axis=1)  # (5,)
        capacities = np.arange(1, 6, dtype=np.float32)
        return (filled_per_row / capacities).astype(np.float32)
    
    def top_n_values(self, arr: np.ndarray, n: int = 3) -> np.ndarray:
        """Efficient extraction of top N values."""
        return np.partition(arr, -n)[-n:].astype(np.float32)

Pros:

    Fast for large arrays (but our arrays are small: 5×5, 5 values, etc.)
    Pythonic, NumPy-idiomatic
    Good if we ever scale to 100+ features

Cons:

    Overkill for 5×5 matrices
    Matrix materialization overhead (small, but non-zero)
    Harder to debug (vectorized operations are less readable)
    Not that much faster for tiny arrays

Option C: Hybrid (Recommended Long-term)

Use Option A for now (clear, testable, maintainable), with a design that allows switching to Option B later if needed:
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    """
    Extract calculated features from game state.
    
    Design allows future optimization via NumPy vectorization without
    changing the public API.
    """
    
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
        self.player = game.players[0]
        self.opponent = game.players[1]
        
        # Will be lazy-computed if needed for perf
        self._my_wall_matrix = None
        self._opp_wall_matrix = None
    
    @property
    def my_wall_matrix(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Lazy-load wall as matrix (for future vectorization)."""
        if self._my_wall_matrix is None:
            self._my_wall_matrix = np.array(self.player.wall, dtype=np.int32)
        return self._my_wall_matrix
    
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        5 values: completion ratio per column.
        
        Currently: simple loop.
        Future: can switch to vectorized np.sum(self.my_wall_matrix, axis=0) / 5.0
        """
        ratios = []
        for col in range(5):
            filled = sum(self.player.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
            ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
        return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # ... rest of methods

Reasoning:

    Start simple (Option A), measure performance
    If encoder is slow (unlikely: 169 features is fast), optimize specific methods
    Most feature calculation is O(5) or O(5×5) anyway — negligible overhead
    Wall time is dominated by AB search and NN forward pass, not encoding

Performance Analysis

Let's estimate overhead:

Scenario: Encoding 10k game positions (gen-0 data collection)

Per position:
  - Original 125 features: ~1 ms (mostly array slicing)
  - 64 new calculated features: ~2 ms (64 simple loops, ~5 operations each)
  - Total: ~3 ms per position
  
10k positions: 10k × 3 ms = 30 seconds

AB search overhead for 10k positions:
  - Each position triggers exhaustive AB search (depth=999, threshold=0)
  - Per position: 10–100 ms average (varies wildly)
  - 10k positions: 100–1000 seconds (real bottleneck!)

Encoding is << 1% of total wall time. Use Option A (clarity).

Verdict: Encoder optimization is not worth the complexity trade-off.
My Recommendation

Use Option A (Feature Extraction Helpers) with this structure:

neural/
├── encoder.py           ← Original flat encoding (125 values)
├── feature_extractor.py ← NEW: FeatureExtractor class (64 values)
└── model.py             ← Unchanged

feature_extractor.py structure:
  class FeatureExtractor:
    def __init__(self, game)
    
    # Tier 1: Columns (14 values)
    def column_completion_ratios(self) → ndarray
    def opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) → ndarray
    def my_max_column_completion(self) → float
    def my_second_max_column_completion(self) → float
    # ... opponent max/2nd-max
    
    # Tier 2: Rows (16 values)
    def row_completion_ratios(self) → ndarray
    def my_top_3_rows(self) → ndarray
    # ... opponent rows
    
    # Tier 4: Pattern lines (30 values)
    def pattern_line_cleanness(self) → ndarray
    def opponent_pattern_line_cleanness(self) → ndarray
    # ... fill ratios, empty next round
    
    # Tier 5: Pattern line flexibility (10 values)
    def incomplete_lines_per_color(self) → ndarray
    def opponent_incomplete_lines_per_color(self) → ndarray
    
    # Tier 6: First-player & game-end (6 values)
    def i_hold_first_player(self) → float
    def opponent_holds_first_player(self) → float
    # ... can end game this round
    
    # Tier 7: Tile availability (10 values)
    # (Already in original encoder, but could refactor here)
    
    # Main method
    def extract_all(self) → ndarray  # Returns all 64 calculated features

encoder.py:
  def _encode_flat_game_tiles(game):
      encoding = np.zeros(189)
      encoding[0:125] = _encode_flat_original_125(game)
      
      extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
      encoding[125:189] = extractor.extract_all()
      
      return encoding

Advantages:

    Clear: Each feature is its own method, easy to understand
    Testable: Test each feature method independently

python

  def test_column_completion():
      game = Game(seed=42)
      game.make_move(...)
      extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
      ratios = extractor.column_completion_ratios()
      assert ratios.shape == (5,)
      assert np.all(ratios >= 0) and np.all(ratios <= 1)

    Maintainable: If we find a bug (e.g., cleanness calculation wrong), it's isolated
    Composable: Easy to add/remove features without touching encoder
    Extensible: Can add extract_columns_only(), extract_rows_only() for debugging
    Performance: No overhead that matters (3 ms per position is fine)

Alternative: If We Really Want Vectorization

If profiling shows encoder is slow (unlikely), we could do this:
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    def __init__(self, game):
        self.game = game
        # Materialize as NumPy once
        self.my_wall = np.array(self.game.players[0].wall, dtype=np.int32)
        self.opp_wall = np.array(self.game.players[1].wall, dtype=np.int32)
    
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        # One-liner vectorized
        return (np.sum(self.my_wall, axis=0) / 5.0).astype(np.float32)
    
    def row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        # Vectorized with broadcasting
        filled = np.sum(self.my_wall, axis=1).astype(np.float32)
        capacities = np.arange(1, 6, dtype=np.float32)
        return (filled / capacities)
    
    def top_n(self, arr: np.ndarray, n: int) -> float:
        """Efficient top-N extraction."""
        if n == 1:
            return float(np.max(arr))
        return float(np.partition(arr, -n)[-n])

This is maybe 10% faster, but adds complexity. Not worth it unless profiling says otherwise.
My Final Answer

Architecture:

    Create neural/feature_extractor.py with FeatureExtractor class
    One method per feature group (columns, rows, cleanness, etc.)
    Single extract_all() method that assembles all 64 features
    In encoder, call FeatureExtractor(game).extract_all() to get features 125–189
    Test each method independently (unit tests in tests/neural/test_feature_extractor.py)

No matrix manipulation needed. Simple loops are clearer and fast enough.

If it gets slow later, we optimize specific methods to vectorized NumPy. But start simple.

Does this approach make sense? Want me to sketch out the full FeatureExtractor class structure with all the methods filled in?
