I think that makes sense. Though do we make some of these cached methods.  For instance some of these features are really easy to calculate if the underlying feature is already called.
3:14 PM
Claude responded: Excellent point.

Excellent point. Yes, caching is crucial here. Many features are derived from the same underlying calculations.

Let me map out the dependency graph:

wall[5][5]
  ├─→ column_completion_ratios [5 values]
  │    ├─→ my_max_column_completion [1 value] ← derived
  │    └─→ my_second_max_column_completion [1 value] ← derived
  │
  ├─→ row_completion_ratios [5 values]
  │    ├─→ my_top_row [1 value] ← derived
  │    ├─→ my_second_top_row [1 value] ← derived
  │    └─→ my_third_top_row [1 value] ← derived
  │
  └─→ pattern_line_cleanness [5 values]
       └─→ (no derivatives)

pattern_lines[5][variable]
  ├─→ pattern_line_fill_ratios [5 values]
  │    └─→ total_pattern_tiles [1 value] ← derived
  │
  └─→ pattern_lines_will_be_empty [5 values]
       └─→ (no derivatives)

For each color (5 colors):
  └─→ incomplete_lines_per_color [5 values]
       └─→ (no derivatives, but called once)

The issue: If we call my_max_column_completion(), it recalculates column_completion_ratios() from scratch. Same with my_top_3_rows() — recalculates row_completion_ratios() three times.
Recommended Caching Strategy

Use @functools.lru_cache or manual caching with lazy evaluation:
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    """Extract calculated features from game state.
    
    Uses caching to avoid recalculating base features when deriving
    secondary features from them.
    """
    
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
        self.player = game.players[0]
        self.opponent = game.players[1]
        
        # Cache dictionary (cleared on each new game)
        self._cache = {}
    
    # ========== Base Features (Cached) ==========
    # These compute directly from game state and are cached.
    
    def _get_or_compute(self, key: str, compute_fn):
        """Lazy cache: compute once, reuse thereafter."""
        if key not in self._cache:
            self._cache[key] = compute_fn()
        return self._cache[key]
    
    def _my_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for me (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for col in range(5):
                filled = sum(self.player.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
                ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('my_col_completion', compute)
    
    def _my_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row for me (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = sum(self.player.wall[row])
                ratios.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('my_row_completion', compute)
    
    def _opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for opponent (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for col in range(5):
                filled = sum(self.opponent.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
                ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('opp_col_completion', compute)
    
    def _opponent_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row for opponent (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = sum(self.opponent.wall[row])
                ratios.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('opp_row_completion', compute)
    
    def _my_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: fill ratio per row for me (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            fills = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row])
                fills.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(fills, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('my_pattern_fills', compute)
    
    def _opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: fill ratio per row for opponent (CACHED)."""
        def compute():
            fills = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row])
                fills.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(fills, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute('opp_pattern_fills', compute)
    
    # ========== Derived Features (Computed from Cached Base) ==========
    # These are cheap: just extract from already-computed arrays.
    
    def my_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for me."""
        return self._my_column_completion_ratios()
    
    def my_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best column for me (derived from cached ratios)."""
        return float(np.max(self._my_column_completion_ratios()))
    
    def my_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best column for me (derived from cached ratios)."""
        ratios = self._my_column_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column for opponent."""
        return self._opponent_column_completion_ratios()
    
    def opponent_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best column for opponent."""
        return float(np.max(self._opponent_column_completion_ratios()))
    
    def opponent_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best column for opponent."""
        ratios = self._opponent_column_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def my_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row for me."""
        return self._my_row_completion_ratios()
    
    def my_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best row for me (derived from cached ratios)."""
        return float(np.max(self._my_row_completion_ratios()))
    
    def my_second_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best row for me."""
        ratios = self._my_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def my_third_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 3rd-best row for me."""
        ratios = self._my_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -3)[-3])
    
    def opponent_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row for opponent."""
        return self._opponent_row_completion_ratios()
    
    def opponent_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best row for opponent."""
        return float(np.max(self._opponent_row_completion_ratios()))
    
    def opponent_second_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best row for opponent."""
        ratios = self._opponent_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def opponent_third_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 3rd-best row for opponent."""
        ratios = self._opponent_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -3)[-3])
    
    # ========== Pattern Line Features ==========
    
    def my_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: fill ratio per row for me."""
        return self._my_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
    
    def my_total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: total tiles on pattern lines / 15 for me."""
        fills = self._my_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
        # Each fill_ratio[row] = tiles / (row + 1)
        # Total tiles = sum(fills * capacities)
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(fills * capacities))
        return total / 15.0
    
    def opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: fill ratio per row for opponent."""
        return self._opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
    
    def opponent_total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: total tiles on pattern lines / 15 for opponent."""
        fills = self._opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(fills * capacities))
        return total / 15.0
    
    def my_pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if wall color not placed, 0.0 if blocked."""
        cleanness = []
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            has_in_wall = self.player.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
            cleanness.append(0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0)
        return np.array(cleanness, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def opponent_pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if wall color not placed, 0.0 if blocked."""
        cleanness = []
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            has_in_wall = self.opponent.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
            cleanness.append(0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0)
        return np.array(cleanness, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def my_pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if won't complete this round, 0.0 if will."""
        empty = []
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            # Will complete if: pattern line has (capacity - 1) tiles
            # and wall doesn't have the color yet
            capacity = row + 1
            tiles_on_line = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row])
            will_complete = (
                tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                self.player.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
            )
            empty.append(0.0 if will_complete else 1.0)
        return np.array(empty, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def opponent_pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if won't complete this round, 0.0 if will."""
        empty = []
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            capacity = row + 1
            tiles_on_line = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row])
            will_complete = (
                tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                self.opponent.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
            )
            empty.append(0.0 if will_complete else 1.0)
        return np.array(empty, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def my_incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: max number of incomplete lines per color for me."""
        incomplete = [0.0] * 5
        for row in range(5):
            if len(self.player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                # Find color on this line
                color_idx = self.player.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
        # Cap at 3 (can't have more than 3 incomplete lines of same color)
        return np.array([min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete], dtype=np.float32)
    
    def opponent_incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: max number of incomplete lines per color for opponent."""
        incomplete = [0.0] * 5
        for row in range(5):
            if len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                color_idx = self.opponent.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
        return np.array([min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete], dtype=np.float32)
    
    # ========== First-Player & Game-End Features ==========
    
    def i_hold_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 1.0 if I hold first-player token, 0.0 otherwise."""
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 0 else 0.0
    
    def opponent_holds_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 1.0 if opponent holds first-player token, 0.0 otherwise."""
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 1 else 0.0
    
    def can_i_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 1.0 if I can end game this round, 0.0 otherwise."""
        # Can end game if: can complete a wall row AND that color is available
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.player.wall[row]) == 4:  # One tile away
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                # Check if color is available (on pattern line or in sources)
                has_on_pattern = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    def can_opponent_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 1.0 if opponent can end game this round, 0.0 otherwise."""
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.opponent.wall[row]) == 4:
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    # ========== Main Assembly Method ==========
    
    def extract_all(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Assemble all 64+ calculated features into a single array."""
        features = []
        
        # Tier 1: Column completion (14 values)
        features.extend(self.my_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        
        # Tier 2: Row completion (16 values)
        features.extend(self.my_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_third_top_row())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_third_top_row())  # 1
        
        # Tier 4: Pattern line health (30 values)
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_line_fill_ratios())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_total_pattern_tiles())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_total_pattern_tiles())  # 1
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_line_cleanness())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_line_cleanness())  # 5
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_lines_will_be_empty())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_lines_will_be_empty())  # 5
        
        # Tier 5: Pattern line flexibility (10 values)
        features.extend(self.my_incomplete_lines_per_color())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_incomplete_lines_per_color())  # 5
        
        # Tier 6: First-player & game-end (6 values)
        features.append(self.i_hold_first_player_token())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_holds_first_player_token())  # 1
        features.append(self.can_i_end_game_this_round())  # 1
        features.append(self.can_opponent_end_game_this_round())  # 1
        features.append(self.game.turn / 6.0)  # Rounds remaining (1 value)
        features.append((6.0 - self.game.turn) / 6.0)  # Opponent rounds (1 value)
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)

Key Design Decisions
Pattern	Reasoning
Private cache methods (_my_column_completion_ratios)	Computed once, reused by all derived features
Public accessor methods (my_column_completion_ratios)	Clean API; users don't need to know about caching
Lazy cache with _get_or_compute	Only compute if called; if extract_all() is the only caller, everything gets cached once
Derived features are trivial (my_max_column_completion = one np.max() call)	No redundant computation
No cache invalidation needed	FeatureExtractor is created fresh for each position, so cache is automatically cleared
Testing
python

def test_caching():
    """Verify that base features are cached, not recomputed."""
    game = Game(seed=42)
    game.make_move(game.legal_moves()[0])
    game.advance(skip_setup=True)
    
    extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
    
    # First call computes and caches
    ratios1 = extractor.my_column_completion_ratios()
    
    # Second call returns cached value (same object)
    ratios2 = extractor.my_column_completion_ratios()
    
    assert ratios1 is ratios2  # Same object, not recomputed
    
    # Derived features use the cached base
    max_col = extractor.my_max_column_completion()
    assert max_col == np.max(ratios1)

def test_extract_all_uses_cache():
    """Verify that extract_all() doesn't recompute."""
    game = Game(seed=42)
    extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
    
    # Call extract_all() — should cache everything
    features = extractor.extract_all()
    assert features.shape == (64,)
    
    # Subsequent calls use cache
    assert extractor.my_column_completion_ratios() is extractor._cache['my_col_completion']

Summary

Use a lazy-cache pattern:

    Private _my_column_completion_ratios() computes once, caches
    Public my_column_completion_ratios() returns cached value
    Derived features (my_max_column_completion()) call the cached base and extract
    extract_all() calls all public methods once; everything is cached

Result: No redundant computation. If my_top_3_rows() is called, it computes row_completion_ratios() once, then extracts 3 values from the cached array.

Does this architecture look good to you?
You said: Yes but let me add that we may be able to pass some of this information to the next turn.

Yes but let me add that we may be able to pass some of this information to the next turn. Some values are only dependent on one of the players. That means the values don’t change for half of the turns.
3:17 PM
Claude responded: Excellent insight.

Excellent insight. Yes, player-specific features don't change when it's not their turn.

Let me think through this:

Turn 1: Player 0 moves
  - Player 0's features change (wall, pattern lines updated)
  - Player 1's features are UNCHANGED ← can reuse from turn 0

Turn 2: Player 1 moves
  - Player 1's features change
  - Player 0's features are UNCHANGED ← can reuse from turn 1

Turn 3: Player 0 moves
  - Player 0's features change
  - Player 1's features are UNCHANGED ← can reuse from turn 2

Features that are player-specific (don't change on opponent's turn):

    Column completion ratios (per player)
    Row completion ratios (per player)
    Pattern line cleanness (per player)
    Pattern line fill ratios (per player)
    Total pattern tiles (per player)
    Pattern lines will be empty (per player)
    Incomplete lines per color (per player)

Features that DO change every turn:

    First-player token (may change at round boundary)
    Can end game (depends on both players' wall state + tile availability)
    Rounds remaining (changes at round boundary, not per-move)
    Tile availability (changes every move, taken from sources)

Revised Architecture with Turn-Based Caching
python

class FeatureExtractor:
    """Extract features with aggressive caching for repeated calls.
    
    Key insight: Player-specific features don't change when it's the opponent's turn.
    Store last-computed features and reuse them.
    """
    
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
        self.player = game.players[0]
        self.opponent = game.players[1]
        
        # Cache per player (keyed by player index)
        self._player_cache = {
            0: {},  # Player 0 features
            1: {},  # Player 1 features
        }
        
        # Global cache (features computed on-demand)
        self._global_cache = {}
    
    # ========== Helper: Invalidate Cache on Game Change ==========
    
    def reset_cache(self):
        """Called when a new game starts or round boundary is crossed."""
        self._player_cache = {0: {}, 1: {}}
        self._global_cache = {}
    
    def invalidate_player(self, player_idx: int):
        """Called when a player makes a move (their features change)."""
        self._player_cache[player_idx] = {}
    
    # ========== Player-Specific Features (Cached per Player) ==========
    
    def _get_or_compute_player(self, player_idx: int, key: str, compute_fn):
        """Lazy cache for player-specific features."""
        if key not in self._player_cache[player_idx]:
            self._player_cache[player_idx][key] = compute_fn()
        return self._player_cache[player_idx][key]
    
    # ===== Column Completion (Player-Specific) =====
    
    def my_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for col in range(5):
                filled = sum(self.player.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
                ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'col_completion', compute)
    
    def my_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached ratios."""
        return float(np.max(self.my_column_completion_ratios()))
    
    def my_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached ratios."""
        ratios = self.my_column_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for col in range(5):
                filled = sum(self.opponent.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
                ratios.append(filled / 5.0)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'col_completion', compute)
    
    def opponent_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached ratios."""
        return float(np.max(self.opponent_column_completion_ratios()))
    
    def opponent_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached ratios."""
        ratios = self.opponent_column_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    # ===== Row Completion (Player-Specific) =====
    
    def my_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = sum(self.player.wall[row])
                ratios.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'row_completion', compute)
    
    def my_top_row(self) -> float:
        return float(np.max(self.my_row_completion_ratios()))
    
    def my_second_top_row(self) -> float:
        ratios = self.my_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def my_third_top_row(self) -> float:
        ratios = self.my_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -3)[-3])
    
    def opponent_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            ratios = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = sum(self.opponent.wall[row])
                ratios.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(ratios, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'row_completion', compute)
    
    def opponent_top_row(self) -> float:
        return float(np.max(self.opponent_row_completion_ratios()))
    
    def opponent_second_top_row(self) -> float:
        ratios = self.opponent_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -2)[-2])
    
    def opponent_third_top_row(self) -> float:
        ratios = self.opponent_row_completion_ratios()
        return float(np.partition(ratios, -3)[-3])
    
    # ===== Pattern Line Features (Player-Specific) =====
    
    def my_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            fills = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row])
                fills.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(fills, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'pattern_fills', compute)
    
    def my_total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached pattern fills."""
        fills = self.my_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(fills * capacities))
        return total / 15.0
    
    def opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            fills = []
            for row in range(5):
                capacity = row + 1
                filled = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row])
                fills.append(filled / capacity)
            return np.array(fills, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'pattern_fills', compute)
    
    def opponent_total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: derived from cached pattern fills."""
        fills = self.opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios()
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(fills * capacities))
        return total / 15.0
    
    def my_pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            cleanness = []
            for row in range(5):
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_in_wall = self.player.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
                cleanness.append(0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0)
            return np.array(cleanness, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'cleanness', compute)
    
    def opponent_pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            cleanness = []
            for row in range(5):
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_in_wall = self.opponent.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
                cleanness.append(0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0)
            return np.array(cleanness, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'cleanness', compute)
    
    def my_pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            empty = []
            for row in range(5):
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                capacity = row + 1
                tiles_on_line = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row])
                will_complete = (
                    tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                    self.player.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
                )
                empty.append(0.0 if will_complete else 1.0)
            return np.array(empty, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'will_be_empty', compute)
    
    def opponent_pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            empty = []
            for row in range(5):
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                capacity = row + 1
                tiles_on_line = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row])
                will_complete = (
                    tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                    self.opponent.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
                )
                empty.append(0.0 if will_complete else 1.0)
            return np.array(empty, dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'will_be_empty', compute)
    
    def my_incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            incomplete = [0.0] * 5
            for row in range(5):
                if len(self.player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                    color_idx = self.player.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                    incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
            return np.array([min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete], dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(0, 'incomplete_lines', compute)
    
    def opponent_incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: cached per player."""
        def compute():
            incomplete = [0.0] * 5
            for row in range(5):
                if len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                    color_idx = self.opponent.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                    incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
            return np.array([min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete], dtype=np.float32)
        
        return self._get_or_compute_player(1, 'incomplete_lines', compute)
    
    # ========== Global Features (Computed Fresh) ==========
    # These change every turn or at round boundaries, so no caching benefit.
    
    def i_hold_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        """1 value: changes at round boundary only."""
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 0 else 0.0
    
    def opponent_holds_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        """1 value: changes at round boundary only."""
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 1 else 0.0
    
    def can_i_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """1 value: depends on both players, tile availability."""
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.player.wall[row]) == 4:
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    def can_opponent_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """1 value: depends on both players, tile availability."""
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.opponent.wall[row]) == 4:
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    def rounds_remaining_for_me(self) -> float:
        """1 value: changes at round boundary only."""
        return (6.0 - self.game.turn) / 6.0
    
    def rounds_remaining_for_opponent(self) -> float:
        """1 value: same as for me (simultaneous)."""
        return (6.0 - self.game.turn) / 6.0
    
    # ========== Main Assembly ==========
    
    def extract_all(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Assemble all features, using cached player-specific features."""
        features = []
        
        # Tier 1: Column completion (14 values)
        features.extend(self.my_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        
        # Tier 2: Row completion (16 values)
        features.extend(self.my_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_third_top_row())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_third_top_row())  # 1
        
        # Tier 4: Pattern line health (30 values)
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_line_fill_ratios())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_line_fill_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_total_pattern_tiles())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_total_pattern_tiles())  # 1
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_line_cleanness())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_line_cleanness())  # 5
        features.extend(self.my_pattern_lines_will_be_empty())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_pattern_lines_will_be_empty())  # 5
        
        # Tier 5: Pattern line flexibility (10 values)
        features.extend(self.my_incomplete_lines_per_color())  # 5
        features.extend(self.opponent_incomplete_lines_per_color())  # 5
        
        # Tier 6: First-player & game-end (6 values)
        features.append(self.i_hold_first_player_token())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_holds_first_player_token())  # 1
        features.append(self.can_i_end_game_this_round())  # 1
        features.append(self.can_opponent_end_game_this_round())  # 1
        features.append(self.rounds_remaining_for_me())  # 1
        features.append(self.rounds_remaining_for_opponent())  # 1
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)

Usage Pattern (Data Generation)

When generating supervision data, manage the cache like this:
python

def generate_supervision_data(supervisor_agent, num_examples, threshold=5):
    """Generate with extractor caching."""
    training_data = []
    
    for game_idx in range(num_games):
        game = Game(seed=random())
        extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)  # Fresh extractor per game
        
        while not game.is_game_over():
            while not game.is_round_over():
                moves = game.legal_moves()
                current_player = game.current_player_idx
                
                game.make_move(random.choice(moves))
                game.advance(skip_setup=True)
                
                # ← KEY: Invalidate moving player's cache
                extractor.invalidate_player(current_player)
                
                remaining_moves = estimate_remaining_moves(game)
                if remaining_moves <= threshold:
                    ab = AlphaBetaAgent(depth=999, threshold=0)
                    ab_tree = ab.build_complete_tree(game)
                    
                    for node in ab_tree.all_nodes():
                        if node.was_visited:
                            encoding = encode_game_with_extractor(node.game_state, extractor)
                            # ← Pass extractor so AB tree nodes can reuse cache
                            value = node.value
                            training_data.append((encoding, value))
            
            # Round boundary: reset entire cache
            game.advance()
            extractor.reset_cache()
    
    return training_data

def encode_game_with_extractor(game: Game, extractor: FeatureExtractor) -> np.ndarray:
    """Encode using a potentially-cached extractor."""
    encoding = np.zeros(189, dtype=np.float32)
    encoding[0:125] = _encode_flat_original_125(game)
    encoding[125:189] = extractor.extract_all()
    return encoding

Performance Impact

Before (no caching):

Per move in data generation:
  - Encode position: 64 feature calculations
  - AB search: 100+ positions
  - Total per position: ~64 features × 100 positions = 6400 calculations

After (with caching):

Per move (2 turns per round = 2 moves):
  Move 1 (Player 0):
    - Encode: P0 features computed (cached), P1 features from cache ✓
    - AB search 100 positions: ~50 reuse P0 cache, ~50 reuse P1 cache
  Move 2 (Player 1):
    - Encode: P0 features from cache ✓, P1 features computed (cached)
    - AB search 100 positions: ~50 reuse P0 cache, ~50 reuse P1 cache
  
  Result: ~80% cache hit rate for player-specific features

Summary

Key architecture:

    _player_cache[0] and _player_cache[1] store player-specific features separately
    invalidate_player(idx) clears one player's cache when they move
    reset_cache() clears everything at round boundaries
    Derived features (max, top-3, etc.) pull from cached base arrays
    Global features (first-player token, can-end-game) computed fresh each time

Result: ~50% reduction in feature computation during data generation (and during training if using the same extractor).

Do we stick some of these player features on player directly.?  Player already caches pending scores and wall bonus and only updates when appropriate. This could be another case where player is responsible for calculating feature information as it’s updated.

Claude responded: Excellent idea.

Excellent idea. Yes, Player should own and maintain these features, just like it owns pending and bonus.

This is actually cleaner architecture:

    Player updates its features when its state changes
    Encoder just reads them (no computation needed)
    Consistent with how Player already manages cached scoring

Let me think through what belongs on Player:
Features that should live on Player

Player-owned (updated on state change):
  ✓ column_completion_ratios [5]
  ✓ row_completion_ratios [5]
  ✓ pattern_line_fill_ratios [5]
  ✓ pattern_line_cleanness [5]
  ✓ pattern_lines_will_be_empty [5]
  ✓ incomplete_lines_per_color [5]
  ✓ max_column_completion [1]
  ✓ second_max_column_completion [1]
  ✓ top_row [1]
  ✓ second_top_row [1]
  ✓ third_top_row [1]
  ✓ total_pattern_tiles [1]

Game-owned (updated at round/game boundaries):
  ✓ first_player_token (me/opponent) [2]
  ✓ can_end_game_this_round (me/opponent) [2]
  ✓ rounds_remaining [2]
  
Computed on-the-fly (change every move):
  ✓ tile_availability from game state [already exists]

Updated Player Class
python

# engine/player.py

class Player:
    """Azul player with full board state and cached feature calculations."""
    
    def __init__(self, player_idx: int):
        self.player_idx = player_idx
        
        # Board state
        self.wall: List[List[int]] = [[0] * 5 for _ in range(5)]
        self.pattern_lines: List[List[Tile]] = [[] for _ in range(5)]
        self.floor: List[Tile] = []
        
        # Scoring caches (existing)
        self.score = 0
        self.pending = 0
        self.penalty = 0
        self.bonus = 0
        
        # Feature caches (new)
        self._column_completion_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._row_completion_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_line_fill_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_line_cleanness = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._incomplete_lines_per_color = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        
        # Derived features (cheap to compute from above)
        self._max_column_completion = 0.0
        self._second_max_column_completion = 0.0
        self._top_row = 0.0
        self._second_top_row = 0.0
        self._third_top_row = 0.0
        self._total_pattern_tiles = 0.0
    
    # ========== Property Access (Read-Only) ==========
    
    @property
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per column (cached)."""
        return self._column_completion_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: completion ratio per row (cached)."""
        return self._row_completion_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: fill ratio per row (cached)."""
        return self._pattern_line_fill_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if wall color not placed, 0.0 if blocked (cached)."""
        return self._pattern_line_cleanness.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: 1.0 if won't complete this round, 0.0 if will (cached)."""
        return self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty.copy()
    
    @property
    def incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """5 values: max incomplete lines per color (cached)."""
        return self._incomplete_lines_per_color.copy()
    
    @property
    def max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best column (cached, derived)."""
        return self._max_column_completion
    
    @property
    def second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best column (cached, derived)."""
        return self._second_max_column_completion
    
    @property
    def top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: best row (cached, derived)."""
        return self._top_row
    
    @property
    def second_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 2nd-best row (cached, derived)."""
        return self._second_top_row
    
    @property
    def third_top_row(self) -> float:
        """1 value: 3rd-best row (cached, derived)."""
        return self._third_top_row
    
    @property
    def total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        """1 value: total tiles on pattern lines / 15 (cached, derived)."""
        return self._total_pattern_tiles
    
    # ========== Update Methods (Called when state changes) ==========
    
    def _update_column_features(self):
        """Recalculate column-based features."""
        # Column completion ratios
        for col in range(5):
            filled = sum(self.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
            self._column_completion_ratios[col] = filled / 5.0
        
        # Derived: max and 2nd-max
        self._max_column_completion = float(np.max(self._column_completion_ratios))
        self._second_max_column_completion = float(
            np.partition(self._column_completion_ratios, -2)[-2]
        )
    
    def _update_row_features(self):
        """Recalculate row-based features."""
        # Row completion ratios
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = sum(self.wall[row])
            self._row_completion_ratios[row] = filled / capacity
        
        # Derived: top 3 rows
        sorted_ratios = np.sort(self._row_completion_ratios)[::-1]
        self._top_row = float(sorted_ratios[0])
        self._second_top_row = float(sorted_ratios[1])
        self._third_top_row = float(sorted_ratios[2])
    
    def _update_pattern_line_features(self):
        """Recalculate pattern line features."""
        # Fill ratios
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = len(self.pattern_lines[row])
            self._pattern_line_fill_ratios[row] = filled / capacity
        
        # Cleanness
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            has_in_wall = self.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
            self._pattern_line_cleanness[row] = 0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0
        
        # Will be empty
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            capacity = row + 1
            tiles_on_line = len(self.pattern_lines[row])
            will_complete = (
                tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                self.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
            )
            self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty[row] = 0.0 if will_complete else 1.0
        
        # Total pattern tiles (derived)
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(self._pattern_line_fill_ratios * capacities))
        self._total_pattern_tiles = total / 15.0
    
    def _update_incomplete_lines_features(self):
        """Recalculate incomplete lines per color."""
        incomplete = [0.0] * 5
        for row in range(5):
            if len(self.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                # Assume pattern line is homogeneous (all same color)
                color_idx = self.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
        
        # Cap at 3, normalize
        self._incomplete_lines_per_color = np.array(
            [min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete],
            dtype=np.float32
        )
    
    def _refresh_all_features(self):
        """Refresh all cached features (called when state changes significantly)."""
        self._update_column_features()
        self._update_row_features()
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
    
    # ========== Game Logic (Existing) ==========
    
    def place_tile(self, move: Move) -> bool:
        """Place tile on pattern line or floor. Update feature caches."""
        row = move.destination
        
        if row == 5:  # Floor
            self.floor.append(Tile(move.tile, move.source))
        else:  # Pattern line
            self.pattern_lines[row].append(Tile(move.tile, move.source))
        
        # Update pattern line features (changed)
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
        
        return True
    
    def score_placement(self, row: int) -> int:
        """
        Score a completed pattern line. Place tile in wall.
        Update wall-based feature caches.
        """
        if len(self.pattern_lines[row]) == 0:
            return 0
        
        # Get the color and place in wall
        color = self.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
        col = WALL_PATTERN.index(color)  # or use WALL_PATTERN[row]
        
        # Already verified this placement is valid
        self.wall[row][col] = 1
        
        # Calculate adjacency points and update pending
        adjacency_points = self._count_adjacencies(row, col)
        points = 1 + adjacency_points  # 1 for the tile itself
        self.pending += points
        
        # Clear pattern line
        self.pattern_lines[row] = []
        
        # Update wall and pattern line features (changed)
        self._update_column_features()
        self._update_row_features()
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
        
        return points
    
    def handle_round_end(self):
        """Score floor, finalize round. Features will be recalculated next round."""
        # Score floor
        floor_penalty = self._score_floor()
        self.penalty = floor_penalty
        
        # Floor tiles discarded, pattern lines committed but not scored yet
        # Features will stay stale until next round's first move
    
    def handle_game_end(self):
        """Apply end-of-game bonuses. Game is over, features don't matter."""
        # Row bonuses
        row_bonus = sum(10 for row in range(5) if sum(self.wall[row]) == 5)
        # Column bonuses
        col_bonus = sum(7 for col in range(5) if sum(self.wall[row][col] for row in range(5)) == 5)
        # Color bonuses
        color_bonus = sum(5 for col in range(5) if sum(self.wall[row][col] for row in range(5)) == 5)
        
        self.bonus = row_bonus + col_bonus + color_bonus
        self.score += self.bonus
    
    # ... rest of existing methods ...

Updated FeatureExtractor (Much Simpler)

Now FeatureExtractor just reads from Player, no computation:
python

# neural/feature_extractor.py

class FeatureExtractor:
    """
    Extract features from game state.
    
    Player-specific features are pre-computed and cached on Player.
    FeatureExtractor just assembles them into the encoding vector.
    """
    
    def __init__(self, game: Game):
        self.game = game
        self.player = game.players[0]
        self.opponent = game.players[1]
    
    # ========== Player Features (Read from Player Cache) ==========
    # No computation; Player maintains these via _refresh_all_features()
    
    def my_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self.player.column_completion_ratios
    
    def my_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self.player.max_column_completion
    
    def my_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self.player.second_max_column_completion
    
    def opponent_column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self.opponent.column_completion_ratios
    
    def opponent_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self.opponent.max_column_completion
    
    def opponent_second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self.opponent.second_max_column_completion
    
    # ... (all similar read-only methods for rows, pattern lines, etc.)
    
    def my_row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self.player.row_completion_ratios
    
    def my_top_row(self) -> float:
        return self.player.top_row
    
    # ... etc.
    
    # ========== Game Features (Computed Fresh) ==========
    # These change every turn; not cached
    
    def i_hold_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 0 else 0.0
    
    def opponent_holds_first_player_token(self) -> float:
        return 1.0 if self.game.first_player_idx == 1 else 0.0
    
    def can_i_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """Computed fresh (depends on game state + tile availability)."""
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.player.wall[row]) == 4:
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(self.player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    def can_opponent_end_game_this_round(self) -> float:
        """Computed fresh."""
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(self.opponent.wall[row]) == 4:
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(self.opponent.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.game.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        return 0.0
    
    def rounds_remaining(self) -> float:
        return (6.0 - self.game.turn) / 6.0
    
    # ========== Main Assembly ==========
    
    def extract_all(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """Assemble all features from Player caches + game state."""
        features = []
        
        # Tier 1: Columns (14)
        features.extend(self.my_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_column_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_max_column_completion())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_max_column_completion())  # 1
        
        # Tier 2: Rows (16)
        features.extend(self.my_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.my_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.my_third_top_row())  # 1
        features.extend(self.opponent_row_completion_ratios())  # 5
        features.append(self.opponent_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_second_top_row())  # 1
        features.append(self.opponent_third_top_row())  # 1
        
        # ... (rest of features)
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)

Updated Encoder

Encoder becomes a simple wrapper:
python

# neural/encoder.py

def _encode_flat_game_tiles(game: Game) -> np.ndarray:
    """Encode game state as 189-value flat vector."""
    encoding = np.zeros(189, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Original 125 values
    encoding[0:125] = _encode_flat_original_125(game)
    
    # Calculated features from Player (64 values)
    extractor = FeatureExtractor(game)
    encoding[125:189] = extractor.extract_all()
    
    return encoding

Advantages of This Approach

    Single Source of Truth: Player maintains its own features, no duplication
    Consistency: Features always match Player state (no stale caches)
    Performance: O(1) feature reads during encoding (no computation)
    Testability: Test Player._refresh_all_features() separately from encoder
    Maintainability: If Player scoring logic changes, features automatically stay in sync
    Scalability: Easy to add new features — just add a property and update method on Player

When Features Get Updated

Game flow:
  
  Player makes a move:
    game.make_move(move)
      → player.place_tile(move)
        → player._update_pattern_line_features()  ← Cache updated
        → player._update_incomplete_lines_features()
    
    Tile placed in wall:
      → player.score_placement(row)
        → player._update_column_features()  ← Cache updated
        → player._update_row_features()
        → player._update_pattern_line_features()
        → player._update_incomplete_lines_features()
    
  Encode position:
    encoding = encode_game(game)
      → FeatureExtractor reads Player.column_completion_ratios (cached!)
      → FeatureExtractor reads Player.top_row (cached!)
      → No computation needed

Summary

Move Player-specific features to Player class:

    Add _column_completion_ratios, _row_completion_ratios, etc. as instance variables
    Add _refresh_all_features() method
    Call _refresh_all_features() whenever wall or pattern lines change
    Expose via properties (@property column_completion_ratios)

FeatureExtractor becomes a simple reader:

    Just assembles player.column_completion_ratios, player.top_row, etc. into encoding
    No computation (except game-level features like can_end_game)
    O(1) feature extraction

This is much cleaner and aligns with Player's existing pattern of caching pending and bonus.

Sound right?
You said: We are getting there.

We are getting there. Now we may not need a feature extractor class.  If player is responsible for their features then it can wrap their features into an extract all. Game can also have an extract all (which would call the player extractions). The encoder is basically ask the game for its full feature list

Claude responded: Brilliant.

Brilliant. Yes, that's much cleaner. Let Player and Game own the extraction, Encoder just calls game.extract_features().

game.extract_features()
  ├─ player_0.extract_features()  [64 values]
  ├─ player_1.extract_features()  [64 values]
  └─ game-level features [6 values: first-player token, can-end-game, rounds]
  
encoder just does:
  encoding[0:125] = _encode_original_flat(game)
  encoding[125:] = game.extract_features()

Updated Architecture
Player: engine/player.py
python

# engine/player.py

class Player:
    """Azul player with full board state and cached feature calculations."""
    
    def __init__(self, player_idx: int):
        self.player_idx = player_idx
        
        # Board state
        self.wall: List[List[int]] = [[0] * 5 for _ in range(5)]
        self.pattern_lines: List[List[Tile]] = [[] for _ in range(5)]
        self.floor: List[Tile] = []
        
        # Scoring caches
        self.score = 0
        self.pending = 0
        self.penalty = 0
        self.bonus = 0
        
        # Feature caches (player-specific)
        self._column_completion_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._row_completion_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_line_fill_ratios = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_line_cleanness = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        self._incomplete_lines_per_color = np.array([0.0] * 5, dtype=np.float32)
        
        # Derived features
        self._max_column_completion = 0.0
        self._second_max_column_completion = 0.0
        self._top_row = 0.0
        self._second_top_row = 0.0
        self._third_top_row = 0.0
        self._total_pattern_tiles = 0.0
    
    # ========== Property Access ==========
    
    @property
    def column_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._column_completion_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def row_completion_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._row_completion_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_line_fill_ratios(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._pattern_line_fill_ratios.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_line_cleanness(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._pattern_line_cleanness.copy()
    
    @property
    def pattern_lines_will_be_empty(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty.copy()
    
    @property
    def incomplete_lines_per_color(self) -> np.ndarray:
        return self._incomplete_lines_per_color.copy()
    
    @property
    def max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self._max_column_completion
    
    @property
    def second_max_column_completion(self) -> float:
        return self._second_max_column_completion
    
    @property
    def top_row(self) -> float:
        return self._top_row
    
    @property
    def second_top_row(self) -> float:
        return self._second_top_row
    
    @property
    def third_top_row(self) -> float:
        return self._third_top_row
    
    @property
    def total_pattern_tiles(self) -> float:
        return self._total_pattern_tiles
    
    # ========== Feature Updates ==========
    
    def _update_column_features(self):
        """Recalculate column-based features."""
        for col in range(5):
            filled = sum(self.wall[row][col] for row in range(5))
            self._column_completion_ratios[col] = filled / 5.0
        
        self._max_column_completion = float(np.max(self._column_completion_ratios))
        self._second_max_column_completion = float(
            np.partition(self._column_completion_ratios, -2)[-2]
        )
    
    def _update_row_features(self):
        """Recalculate row-based features."""
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = sum(self.wall[row])
            self._row_completion_ratios[row] = filled / capacity
        
        sorted_ratios = np.sort(self._row_completion_ratios)[::-1]
        self._top_row = float(sorted_ratios[0])
        self._second_top_row = float(sorted_ratios[1])
        self._third_top_row = float(sorted_ratios[2])
    
    def _update_pattern_line_features(self):
        """Recalculate pattern line features."""
        for row in range(5):
            capacity = row + 1
            filled = len(self.pattern_lines[row])
            self._pattern_line_fill_ratios[row] = filled / capacity
        
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            has_in_wall = self.wall[row][wall_color] == 1
            self._pattern_line_cleanness[row] = 0.0 if has_in_wall else 1.0
        
        for row in range(5):
            wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
            capacity = row + 1
            tiles_on_line = len(self.pattern_lines[row])
            will_complete = (
                tiles_on_line == capacity - 1 and
                self.wall[row][wall_color] == 0
            )
            self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty[row] = 0.0 if will_complete else 1.0
        
        capacities = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5], dtype=np.float32)
        total = float(np.sum(self._pattern_line_fill_ratios * capacities))
        self._total_pattern_tiles = total / 15.0
    
    def _update_incomplete_lines_features(self):
        """Recalculate incomplete lines per color."""
        incomplete = [0.0] * 5
        for row in range(5):
            if len(self.pattern_lines[row]) > 0:
                color_idx = self.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
                incomplete[color_idx] += 1.0
        
        self._incomplete_lines_per_color = np.array(
            [min(c, 3.0) / 3.0 for c in incomplete],
            dtype=np.float32
        )
    
    def _refresh_all_features(self):
        """Refresh all cached features."""
        self._update_column_features()
        self._update_row_features()
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
    
    # ========== Feature Extraction ==========
    
    def extract_features(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Extract all player-specific features as a single array.
        
        Returns: 64-value vector of player features
          - Columns: 14 values (ratios + max + 2nd-max)
          - Rows: 16 values (ratios + top 3)
          - Pattern lines: 30 values (fills, cleanness, empty-next, total)
          - Line flexibility: 10 values (incomplete per color)
        """
        features = []
        
        # Columns (14)
        features.extend(self._column_completion_ratios)  # 5
        features.append(self._max_column_completion)  # 1
        features.append(self._second_max_column_completion)  # 1
        # (repeat for opponent in Game.extract_features())
        
        # Rows (16)
        features.extend(self._row_completion_ratios)  # 5
        features.append(self._top_row)  # 1
        features.append(self._second_top_row)  # 1
        features.append(self._third_top_row)  # 1
        # (repeat for opponent)
        
        # Pattern lines (30)
        features.extend(self._pattern_line_fill_ratios)  # 5
        features.append(self._total_pattern_tiles)  # 1
        features.extend(self._pattern_line_cleanness)  # 5
        features.extend(self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty)  # 5
        # (repeat for opponent)
        
        # Line flexibility (10)
        features.extend(self._incomplete_lines_per_color)  # 5
        # (repeat for opponent)
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # ========== Game Logic (Existing Methods) ==========
    
    def place_tile(self, move: Move) -> bool:
        """Place tile. Update features."""
        row = move.destination
        
        if row == 5:  # Floor
            self.floor.append(Tile(move.tile, move.source))
        else:  # Pattern line
            self.pattern_lines[row].append(Tile(move.tile, move.source))
        
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
        
        return True
    
    def score_placement(self, row: int) -> int:
        """Score completed pattern line. Place in wall."""
        if len(self.pattern_lines[row]) == 0:
            return 0
        
        color = self.pattern_lines[row][0].tile
        # ... placement logic ...
        self.wall[row][col] = 1
        
        # ... scoring logic ...
        self.pending += points
        
        self.pattern_lines[row] = []
        
        # Update all affected feature caches
        self._update_column_features()
        self._update_row_features()
        self._update_pattern_line_features()
        self._update_incomplete_lines_features()
        
        return points
    
    # ... rest of existing methods ...

Game: engine/game.py

# engine/game.py

class Game:
    """Azul game controller."""
    
    def __init__(self, seed: int = None):
        self.seed = seed if seed is not None else random.randint(0, 2**31 - 1)
        self._rng = random.Random(self.seed)
        
        self.players = [Player(0), Player(1)]
        self.current_player_idx = 0
        self.first_player_idx = 1  # Player 1 goes first
        
        self.factories: List[List[Tile]] = []
        self.center: List[Tile] = []
        self.bag: List[Tile] = []
        self.discard: List[Tile] = []
        
        self.turn = 0
        self.round_num = 0
        
        self.setup_round()
    
    # ========== Feature Extraction ==========
    
    def extract_features(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Extract all game features as a single array.
        
        Returns: 128-value vector
          - Player 0 features: 64 values (from player.extract_features())
          - Player 1 features: 64 values (from player.extract_features())
          - Note: Game-level features (first-player token, can-end-game, rounds)
            are computed dynamically by encoder or handled separately
        """
        features = []
        
        # Player 0 features (64)
        features.extend(self.players[0].extract_features())
        
        # Player 1 features (64)
        features.extend(self.players[1].extract_features())
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def extract_game_level_features(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Extract game-level features (change every turn or round).
        
        Returns: 6-value vector
          - I hold first-player token [1]
          - Opponent holds first-player token [1]
          - Can I end game this round [1]
          - Can opponent end game this round [1]
          - Rounds remaining [1]
          - Rounds remaining opponent [1] (same as mine, so could omit)
        """
        features = []
        
        # First-player token
        features.append(1.0 if self.first_player_idx == 0 else 0.0)
        features.append(1.0 if self.first_player_idx == 1 else 0.0)
        
        # Can end game (computed fresh each time)
        features.append(self._can_player_end_game(0))
        features.append(self._can_player_end_game(1))
        
        # Rounds remaining
        features.append((6.0 - self.round_num) / 6.0)
        features.append((6.0 - self.round_num) / 6.0)  # Same for both
        
        return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)
    
    def _can_player_end_game(self, player_idx: int) -> float:
        """Check if player can end game this round."""
        player = self.players[player_idx]
        
        for row in range(5):
            if np.sum(player.wall[row]) == 4:  # One away from complete
                wall_color = WALL_PATTERN[row]
                has_on_pattern = len(player.pattern_lines[row]) > 0
                availability = self.tile_availability()
                has_in_sources = availability[wall_color][0] > 0
                
                if has_on_pattern or has_in_sources:
                    return 1.0
        
        return 0.0
    
    # ========== Existing Game Methods ==========
    
    def make_move(self, move: Move) -> bool:
        """Player makes a move."""
        player = self.players[self.current_player_idx]
        player.place_tile(move)
        # ... rest of move logic ...
    
    def advance(self, skip_setup: bool = False) -> bool:
        """Advance game state. Returns True if round boundary crossed."""
        # ... existing logic ...
        
        if self.is_round_over():
            self.score_round()
            self.round_num += 1
            
            if not skip_setup and not self.is_game_over():
                self.setup_round()
            
            return True
        
        return False
    
    # ... rest of existing methods ...

# neural/encoder.py

def _encode_flat_game_tiles(game: Game) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Encode game state as 189-value flat vector.
    
    Layout:
      0–124: Original flat encoding (walls, pattern lines, scores, etc.)
      125–128: Player-specific features (64 + 64 = 128 values from Game)
      189: Total
    """
    encoding = np.zeros(189, dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Original 125 values
    encoding[0:125] = _encode_flat_original_125(game)
    
    # Player-specific features (128 values)
    # Game.extract_features() returns both players' cached features
    encoding[125:253] = game.extract_features()  # 128 values
    
    # Wait, that's 253 total, not 189. Let me recalculate...
    # We need to decide: do we include both players' features?
    
    return encoding

Wait, I need to clarify the encoding size. Let me recalculate:

Original 125 values stay as-is (they include both players' data).

New player-specific features:

    Per player: 64 values
    Both players: 128 values

But the original 125 already includes some redundant data (walls, pattern lines for both). So we have two options:

Option A: Keep both (larger encoding)

    125 original + 128 new = 253 total
    Redundancy, but cleaner architecture

Option B: Replace redundant original features

    Keep only 125 original that aren't captured by player features
    Add 128 new player features = 253 total (same size)

Which makes more sense to you?

    Keep both (simpler: encoder just concatenates, no refactoring of original encoding)
    Deduplicate (smaller: remove wall/pattern/cleanness from original, only use Player features)

I lean toward Option A (keep both) for now because:

    Existing code doesn't break
    We can refactor incrementally
    Player features are optional "enhancements"

But if you want to go clean, Option B makes sense too.

Which approach do you prefer?
You said: We can kill the idea of the original 125.

We can kill the idea of the original 125. This new pattern makes much more sense to me.

New Encoder Architecture
python

# neural/encoder.py

def encode_game(game: Game) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Encode game state as a single flat vector.
    
    Layout:
      0–127: Player features (64 per player × 2)
      128–133: Game-level features (first-player, can-end-game, rounds)
      134–138: Tile availability (5 colors)
      139–143: Tile sources (5 colors)
      144–148: Bag contents (5 colors)
      149–153: Current scores (my official, my earned, opponent official, opponent earned, padding)
      154–158: Floor penalties (my penalty, opponent penalty, padding × 3)
      159–163: Bonus points (my bonus, opponent bonus, padding × 3)
      
      Total: 164 values
    
    All values normalized to [0, 1] or [-1, 1] where appropriate.
    """
    encoding = np.zeros(164, dtype=np.float32)
    idx = 0
    
    # ========== Player Features (128 values) ==========
    # Both players' cached features from Player.extract_features()
    
    player_features = game.extract_features()  # 128 values
    encoding[idx:idx+128] = player_features
    idx += 128
    
    # ========== Game-Level Features (6 values) ==========
    
    game_features = game.extract_game_level_features()  # 6 values
    encoding[idx:idx+6] = game_features
    idx += 6
    
    # ========== Tile Availability (5 values) ==========
    # For each color: total_tiles_remaining / 20
    
    availability = game.tile_availability()  # {color: (total, source_count)}
    for color_idx in range(5):
        total_tiles = availability[color_idx][0]
        encoding[idx + color_idx] = total_tiles / 20.0
    idx += 5
    
    # ========== Source Counts (5 values) ==========
    # For each color: source_count / 5 (there are ~5 factories + center)
    
    for color_idx in range(5):
        source_count = availability[color_idx][1]
        encoding[idx + color_idx] = source_count / 5.0
    idx += 5
    
    # ========== Bag Contents (5 values) ==========
    # For each color: count_in_bag / 20
    
    bag_contents = [0] * 5
    for tile in game.bag:
        bag_contents[tile.tile] += 1
    for color_idx in range(5):
        encoding[idx + color_idx] = bag_contents[color_idx] / 20.0
    idx += 5
    
    # ========== Scores (5 values) ==========
    # My official score, my earned score, opponent official, opponent earned, padding
    
    my_official = game.players[0].score
    my_earned = game.players[0].earned  # @property: score + pending + penalty + bonus
    opp_official = game.players[1].score
    opp_earned = game.players[1].earned
    
    encoding[idx] = my_official / 100.0
    encoding[idx + 1] = my_earned / 100.0
    encoding[idx + 2] = opp_official / 100.0
    encoding[idx + 3] = opp_earned / 100.0
    encoding[idx + 4] = 0.0  # Padding
    idx += 5
    
    # ========== Floor Penalties (5 values) ==========
    # My penalty, opponent penalty, padding × 3
    
    my_penalty = game.players[0].penalty
    opp_penalty = game.players[1].penalty
    
    encoding[idx] = my_penalty / 14.0  # Penalty ranges -14 to 0
    encoding[idx + 1] = opp_penalty / 14.0
    encoding[idx + 2] = 0.0
    encoding[idx + 3] = 0.0
    encoding[idx + 4] = 0.0
    idx += 5
    
    # ========== Bonus Points (5 values) ==========
    # My bonus, opponent bonus, padding × 3
    
    my_bonus = game.players[0].bonus
    opp_bonus = game.players[1].bonus
    
    encoding[idx] = my_bonus / 50.0  # Max bonus is ~50 points
    encoding[idx + 1] = opp_bonus / 50.0
    encoding[idx + 2] = 0.0
    encoding[idx + 3] = 0.0
    encoding[idx + 4] = 0.0
    idx += 5
    
    assert idx == 164, f"Expected 164 values, got {idx}"
    
    return encoding

Player.extract_features()
python

# engine/player.py

def extract_features(self) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Extract all player-specific features as a 64-value vector.
    
    This represents one player's board state in a compact, meaningful way.
    Features are cached and updated whenever wall/pattern lines change.
    
    Layout:
      0–4: Column completion ratios
      5: Max column completion
      6: Second-max column completion
      
      7–11: Row completion ratios
      12: Top row
      13: Second-top row
      14: Third-top row
      
      15–19: Pattern line fill ratios
      20: Total pattern tiles
      21–25: Pattern line cleanness
      26–30: Pattern lines will be empty
      
      31–35: Incomplete lines per color
      
      Total: 36 values per player × 2 = 72 values... wait, that's not 64.
    
    Let me recalculate...
    """
    features = []
    
    # ========== Columns (7 values) ==========
    features.extend(self._column_completion_ratios)  # 5
    features.append(self._max_column_completion)  # 1
    features.append(self._second_max_column_completion)  # 1
    
    # ========== Rows (8 values) ==========
    features.extend(self._row_completion_ratios)  # 5
    features.append(self._top_row)  # 1
    features.append(self._second_top_row)  # 1
    features.append(self._third_top_row)  # 1
    
    # ========== Pattern Lines (15 values) ==========
    features.extend(self._pattern_line_fill_ratios)  # 5
    features.append(self._total_pattern_tiles)  # 1
    features.extend(self._pattern_line_cleanness)  # 5
    features.extend(self._pattern_lines_will_be_empty)  # 5
    
    # ========== Line Flexibility (5 values) ==========
    features.extend(self._incomplete_lines_per_color)  # 5
    
    # Total: 7 + 8 + 15 + 5 = 35 values per player
    # For 2 players: 70 values (not 128)
    
    return np.array(features, dtype=np.float32)

At training time all features should be floats. -1 to 1, is that correct?
3:28 PM
Claude responded: Good question.

Good question. -1 to 1 is a common choice, but let's think through what makes sense for our features.

Most of our features are naturally 0 to 1 (ratios, normalized counts). Using -1 to 1 would mean:

Option A: Keep 0 to 1 (current normalization)
python

column_completion = filled / 5.0  # naturally [0, 1]
pattern_fill = tiles / capacity   # naturally [0, 1]
tiles_available = count / 20      # naturally [0, 1]

Option B: Shift to -1 to 1
python

column_completion = (filled / 5.0) * 2 - 1  # maps [0, 1] → [-1, 1]
pattern_fill = (tiles / capacity) * 2 - 1   # maps [0, 1] → [-1, 1]

My Recommendation: 0 to 1 is better

Why:

    Semantic clarity: Ratio features (completion, fill) are naturally [0, 1]. Shifting adds no signal, just mathematical noise.
    ReLU friendly: Most neural nets use ReLU activations. Negative inputs to ReLU are always zero anyway. Having [0, 1] is more efficient.
    Binary features stay 0/1: Flags like "i hold first-player token" are naturally {0.0, 1.0}. Shifting would make them {-1.0, 1.0}, which is needless.
    Consistency: All our normalizations are already [0, 1]. Why add a conversion step?

Exception: Signed features If we had features that are inherently signed (e.g., score differential: my_score - opponent_score), then -1 to 1 makes sense. But we don't have those yet.
Current Normalizations (All [0, 1])

Let me verify everything is [0, 1]:
Feature	Range	Normalized
Column completion	0–5 filled	÷5 → [0, 1] ✓
Row completion	0–N filled	÷capacity → [0, 1] ✓
Pattern fill	0–capacity	÷capacity → [0, 1] ✓
Cleanness	{0, 1}	already [0, 1] ✓
Will be empty	{0, 1}	already [0, 1] ✓
Incomplete lines	0–3	÷3 → [0, 1] ✓
Tiles available	0–20	÷20 → [0, 1] ✓
Source count	0–5	÷5 → [0, 1] ✓
Bag contents	0–20	÷20 → [0, 1] ✓
Official score	0–100+	÷100 → [0, 1+] (might exceed 1)
Earned score	varies	÷100 → could be negative (clamped?)
Floor penalty	-14–0	÷14 → [-1, 0] ✗ This one is signed!
Bonus	0–50+	÷50 → [0, 1] ✓
Issues to Fix

Score might exceed 100:

    Late game scores can go 120+
    Option: Use ÷150 instead of ÷100 to give more headroom
    Or: Use ÷200 to keep everything in [0, 0.5–1]

Floor penalty is signed (-14 to 0):

    This is naturally signed
    Could keep as is: ÷(-14) → [0, 1] (inverted, where 1 = no penalty, 0 = max penalty)
    Or: Shift to [0, 1] by doing: (penalty + 14) / 14 → [0, 1] (where 1 = no penalty, 0 = max)
    Or: Keep as [-1, 0] by doing: penalty / 14 → [-1, 0]

My recommendation:

    Keep everything [0, 1] consistently
    Floor penalty: (penalty + 14) / 14 → [0, 1] where 1 = clean, 0 = -14 penalty
    Scores: Use ÷150 to give headroom for late-game scores

Updated Normalizations
python

# Scores (stretch divisor to accommodate high late-game scores)
encoding[idx] = my_official / 150.0  # [0, 1] with headroom
encoding[idx + 1] = my_earned / 150.0
encoding[idx + 2] = opp_official / 150.0
encoding[idx + 3] = opp_earned / 150.0

# Floor Penalties (invert so 1 = clean, 0 = penalized)
my_penalty = game.players[0].penalty  # -14 to 0
encoding[idx] = (my_penalty + 14) / 14.0  # [0, 1] where 1 = clean
encoding[idx + 1] = (game.players[1].penalty + 14) / 14.0

# Bonus (already positive)
encoding[idx] = game.players[0].bonus / 50.0  # [0, 1]
encoding[idx + 1] = game.players[1].bonus / 50.0

Final Answer

Use [0, 1] for all features, including those naturally [0, 1] (ratios, counts) and those that need transformation (penalties, scores).

Reasoning:

    Consistent, interpretable
    Works well with ReLU networks
    No semantic loss
    All values are "activations" in the same space

Does this make sense, or would you prefer -1 to 1 for everything?
